Important News Two

Gaoming Ferry in Guangzhou Bombed by Bandits 57

Guangzhou Correspondence. At 12:40 this morning, a loud noise suddenly rang out near Renji Street on the West Bund, startling everyone. At that time, pedestrians in the Bund area suspected that a bomb had exploded and ran away in a panic, which was very embarrassing. The order was restored after a while. After investigation, it was found that the Lianxing Ferry, which shuttled between the provincial capital and Gaoming, was bombed by bandits with a water mine. Recently, the bandits of Luo Ji Hong in Sanshan Shibi and Wei Yong Panpu have gathered in this area, specializing in collecting waterway tolls from the ferries to the West River. If they refuse to pay, they will be subjected to various kinds of sabotage. The ferry has repeatedly received letters from the Luo Ji Hong bandits demanding 5,000 yuan for each trip to Xizhihang and 20 yuan for each trip. The ferry refused to pay and, for self-defense, built gun emplacements with eight-tenths of an inch thick steel plates in the Gaoming small wheel and the ferry and installed eight earth cannons and various sharp guns and hired 24 gunners to prepare to resist the bandits. They were also afraid that the bandits would bomb them with water mines, so they used a grab-type Woji wire mesh to arrange them at both ends of the towline to prevent water mines. The bandits saw that the ferry had set up such strict defenses, so they put up white flags all over the riverbank along Sanshan with the words "Special to Fight the Tiger Boat, Gaoming Lianxing Ferry" written on them, and they fluttered in the wind. They also sent a letter to the ferry on the 14th as a final warning, limiting them to prepare 5,000 yuan within three days, otherwise they would treat them with water mines. The ferry laughed it off after receiving the letter. The bandits hated them even more. At 3:00 PM yesterday, the ferry arrived in the provincial capital from the countryside and berthed at the Hadan Pier, preparing to leave the province at 1:00 AM that night to return to the countryside. At about 7:00 PM, a woman in rural clothes carried a rattan bag to take the ferry. When she got off the ferry, she deliberately threw the rattan bag into the river and shouted that she had lost her luggage and fell into the water. At that time, a man who looked like a coolie stood on the dock and, seeing this situation, jumped into the river, saying that he would find the rattan bag for the woman. It took about 20 minutes before he went ashore and said that he could not find it. It was later speculated that the woman and the man were probably sent by the bandits, and the rattan bag contained a water mine. The man who swam into the river to find the rattan bag was the one who went into the water to set up the water mine. When the water mine exploded, it was on the left side of the pier (that is, the left side of the ferry's kitchen), piercing a huge hole, about four feet wide. Behind the ferry's kitchen was the women's cabin. Fortunately, the ferry had not yet departed at this time, so there were only a few people in the kitchen, such as boat companion Wang Sandi. Wang and others only suffered minor injuries to their hands and legs. At that time, the entire ship entered the water, and about 300 male and female passengers scrambled to get ashore, trampling on each other, and many were squeezed into the water. The Jinghai and Taiping sub-bureaus reported this and immediately led the bureau members and armed police to rush to the scene. They first closed the iron gate of the dock. The Tianji Public Security Bureau fire engine rushed to the scene and immediately ordered the firefighters and police to first rescue the male and female passengers and put them on the dock to wait, and sent police to monitor them in order to search them separately. The search was completed until about 4:00 AM, and no suspects were found. Then the iron gate was opened. As for the ferry, after being bombed, it gradually sank. Fortunately, the water there was shallow, and it only sank to the helm house on the deck, with the bow facing south and the stern facing north. The ferry has now hired several boats to start winding the ferry to facilitate the hospital also sent a corpse collection team, and took several small boats, drove to the bay stop point where the ferry was parked to collect corpses, but by 12 o'clock before, still have not found the bodies, according to the ferry inside the people, said, was injured about 10 people, but not very important, was squeezed into the water and drowned male and female passengers, at most but five people cloud (17th).

Restoration of Telecommunications Rights for the Eastern Railway to Original State 58

The Communications Committee Presents Six Proposals

The Board of Supervisors Meeting on the 18th Yields No Results

An Associated Press dispatch from Harbin on the 18th reports that the Northeast Communications Committee entrusted Mo Teh-hui to present an opinion to the board of directors of the Eastern Railway regarding the restoration of telecommunications rights. Apart from the Communications Committee's concession to allow the handover for the restoration of the telecommunications rights to their original state, the opinion includes six items: 1) A contract for paid interconnection between the railway's telegraph and local telegraph services should be established, with the Chinese telegraph bureau paying the railway bureau for interconnection fees, thereby canceling the previous contract where China entrusted the Eastern Railway with the rights to issue telegrams. 2) China is permitted to establish its own telegraph bureau between the A and B telegraph offices of the railway to send and receive commercial telegrams. Even if China cannot implement this immediately, the right is reserved for the future and remains permanently valid. 3) China can set up telegraph bureaus on both sides of the border at Manchuria and Suifenhe. Outgoing telegrams from the Eastern Railway must take the most economical route and be released after inspection. Even if China cannot implement this immediately, the right is reserved for the future and remains permanently valid. 4) All telegraph account balances during the Eastern Railway's period of occupation must be thoroughly investigated by officials dispatched by the Chinese telecommunications authorities, and any surplus must be returned to China. 5) The number of Chinese and Russian personnel in the telecommunications department and telegraph offices must be equal. The telegraph trainees currently recruited by the Chinese telegraph bureau must be given priority in filling vacancies. 6) The telecommunications rights conference must be convened no later than one month after the return of assets.

At 1 a.m. on the 18th, a joint meeting of the directors and supervisors of the Eastern Railway was held to discuss this issue. Chinese and Russian directors and supervisors attended in full. Previously, at the directors' regular meeting on the 17th, both sides had exchanged views on this matter and had some discussions on the method for restoring the telecommunications rights to their original state, but no decision was made. At the meeting on the 18th, the primary issue of handover was first decided to be implemented on the 20th to restore the original state. Subsequently, Mo Teh-hui presented the Communications Committee's opinions and requested discussion. The Russian supervisors and directors did not fully agree with the three items: setting up telegraph bureaus in Manchuria and Suifenhe, China establishing telegraph bureaus between the A and B telegraph offices, and investigating the telegraph fee accounts. As these were not proposals at the time, both sides avoided debate. Finally, the matter was reserved for discussion at the regular meeting on the 21st. On the Communications Committee's side, instructions were recently received from the central government that no concessions would be made on matters of sovereignty under any circumstances. However, whether or not the telecommunications rights conference would be convened would depend on the Russian side's attitude towards the Communications Committee's six proposals. Li Deyan, Deputy Director of the Postal and Telecommunications Department, is still waiting for news in Harbin regarding this matter. However, now that the restoration to the original state has been achieved, the Russian side seems to have no intention of convening the conference.

Work of the Yangtze River Management Committee 59

The Yangtze River originates from the Min Mountains, spanning over 9,000 li. All areas along its basin are important towns. However, in recent years, turbulent floods and slow sediment accumulation have obstructed navigation channels and inundated farmland, causing losses for farmers, merchants, and the people, the magnitude of which is difficult to calculate. Li Zhonggong of the Ministry of Communications' Yangtze River Waterway Management Committee, recognizing this issue, had already planned and completed the surveying of the entire river to prepare for active dredging. Now, in the spirit of the era of material construction, every effort should be made to progress rapidly to achieve the goals. Therefore, he ordered Kong Xiangrong, the Chief of the General Affairs Department, and Song Xishang, the Chief of the Engineering Department, to draft various plans to complete surveying, prepare for construction, and concentrate efforts to improve internal affairs, so that rectification can proceed smoothly and the results can be remarkable in the future, setting a precedent for water conservancy throughout the country.

Complete the Measurement of the First Major Section of Silt Within a Deadline: The Yangtze River from Wusong to Hankou is divided into the first major section. During the winter and spring when the water level drops and the river dries up, the eleven most silted and navigation-obstructing locations are Chongwen Island, Taizi Islet, Yaojia Island, Zhangjia Island, Jiangjia Island, Liang Island, Huguang Sandbar, Daijia Island, Luo Island, Yadan Island, and Desheng Island. Other locations such as Heisha Island, Xinzhou, Dongliu Waterway, Yejia Island, and Madang are also showing a trend of increasing siltation. Since expanding the surveying team last year, the Yangtze River Management Committee has been focusing on surveying. Now, a deadline has been set for completing all surveys by the summer of this year to proceed with dredging projects. Survey team members are also restricted from taking leave arbitrarily and are required to work actively to avoid wasting time and to complete the surveying plan as soon as possible.

Preparing the Jing River Project in Hubei: The Jing River basin in Hubei Province has suffered from river water backflow disasters for many years. The disaster-stricken area in counties such as Jiayu covers 61 square kilometers, or approximately 91,500 acres. Farmers fear the unpredictability of floods and the uncertainty of harvests, often abandoning their land and not daring to plant crops. Weeds and desolate smoke fill the landscape. Every year when floods approach, people leave their homes together, and the magnitude of the losses is truly unbearable. Song Xishang, Chief of the Engineering Department of the Yangtze River Management Committee, drafted a plan for the Jing River Management Project in Hubei, which was submitted by the Ministry of Communications to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation. After the implementation of this plan, not only can the harm of river water backflow be eliminated, but the swampy land can also be transformed into fertile soil. It is estimated that the annual benefits will include a land value of over 39 million yuan and an agricultural output income of over 3.9 million yuan per year. The convenience of transportation will also bring significant benefits. Li Zhonggong, the Chairman of the Committee, is currently contacting the central government and the Hubei Provincial Government separately to proceed with implementation and has ordered the General Engineering and Engineering Departments of the Committee to convene meetings to discuss fundraising methods and construction steps. Song Xishang, the Chief of the Engineering Department of the Committee, is currently planning all projects and is extremely busy.

Expanding the Committee's Headquarters and Centralizing Operations: The Committee originally had an office in Shanghai, where all operations were overseen by the Chief Surveying Engineer, an American named Stowe. However, the mailing of drawings and the receipt of instructions for engineering plans were inconvenient. Therefore, for the sake of centralizing operations, Li Zhonggong, the Chairman of the Yangtze River Management Committee, ordered the General Engineering and Engineering Departments to move the Shanghai office to the Beijing headquarters at the beginning of this month, renting additional rooms to expand office space. He also transferred capable personnel stationed in Shanghai, such as Jia Xiangtuo, Zhao Duanyuan, Liu Dazheng, and Zhang Jingyi, to the General Engineering and Engineering Departments to serve and work. It is reported that additional technical specialists will be recruited to prepare for surveying and construction arrangements.

Reorganization of the Mongolian Banner Military System in Suiyuan Province 60

A dispatch from Suiyuan reports that the thirteen banners of the Ulanqab and Ih Ju leagues each have Mongolian guerrilla units, all of which are cavalry, brave and skilled in battle, and still retain the spirit of nomadic peoples. They are quite effective in protecting the local area and suppressing bandits and rebels. However, their organization is too unsystematic, and their firearms are mostly outdated and lacking. The provincial government and the garrison headquarters both believe that there is a need for reorganization. With prior approval, these units have been reorganized into Mongolian Banner Security Forces, with the garrison commander responsible for handling the matter. The league heads of both leagues have been appointed as commanders of their respective league's security forces, both under the command and supervision of the garrison commander, to achieve unification. The battalion commanders of each banner are concurrently filled by the Jasags of each banner to facilitate deployment. Recent surveys indicate that the Jungar Banner of the Ih Ju League can field 600 cavalrymen, while the Darat Banner, Etok Banner, and Ushing Banner can each field 300 men. The County Prince Banner and Hanggin Banner can each field 200 men, and the Jasag Banner can field 100 men. The Darkhan Banner of the Ulanqab League can field 400 cavalrymen, the Siziwang Banner can field 300 men, the Urad Front Banner can field 300 men, the Central Banner can field 500 men, the Rear Banner can field 200 men, and the Maoming'an Banner can field 100 men. In total, the thirteen banners can field 3,800 men, a force that cannot be considered insignificant. If these forces can be effectively reorganized, they will not only provide local security but also contribute to national defense. It is reported that the garrison headquarters has drafted a general plan for reorganization, which will likely be implemented soon. The content of the plan is quite detailed regarding organization, uniforms, firearms, salaries, and training, and it is mostly tailored to the circumstances of the Mongolian banners. The league heads of both leagues have already received their appointment certificates, and the banners are clamoring for the replenishment of firearms and ammunition. Future results can be confidently predicted. The outline of the plan is recorded below.

General Plan for Reorganizing Mongolian Troops: 1) Purpose: An investigation reveals that the Mongolian troops are scattered across various banners and lack education. In peacetime, they each seek their own livelihood, and in times of trouble, they fight individually. They lack a unified spirit and a command system. It is estimated that the two leagues and thirteen banners have no fewer than 3,000 to 4,000 fully equipped men. If they can be reorganized and trained, they can easily be transformed into elite troops. Moreover, the Suiyuan region is a mixed area of Han and Mongol peoples, and bandits emerge endlessly. To fundamentally eradicate them, it is essential for Han and Mongol peoples to unite to achieve effective results. For the sake of improvement and reorganization, it is proposed to revise the organizational regulations, organize into teams according to the banners, and add training to unite the spirit and unify actions, so that they can be transformed into disciplined and systematic troops, in order to suppress banditry and consolidate border defense. 2) Name: All Mongolian troops reorganized from the banners of the Ulanqab and Ih Ju leagues will be named Mongolian Banner Security Forces. 3) Organization: An investigation reveals that the current number of Mongolian troops in each banner of the Ulanqab and Ih Ju leagues varies from just over one hundred to one thousand. In order to implement a policy of elite troops, a moderate organization is adopted, so that each banner can be organized according to its actual situation, without exceeding the original quota of soldiers, and it is easy to implement. Each banner sets up one or several companies according to the situation, with the princes of each banner concurrently serving as company commanders, referred to as the Nth Company of the Security Force of a certain banner. Each company is composed of four platoons, with numbers attached such as the First Platoon and the Second Platoon. The number of platoons within each company can also be reduced according to the circumstances of each banner, but the number must not be reduced to less than two platoons. Each platoon is composed of three squads, each with one squad leader and seven Mongolian soldiers, numbered in order from the First Squad to the Twelfth Squad for the entire company. If a banner has more than two companies, they will be organized into a battalion, with a battalion commander in charge, referred to as the Nth Battalion of the Security Force of a certain banner, with the dukes of each banner concurrently serving as battalion commanders. The position of company commander in the battalion will be filled by military officers, but each battalion must not exceed three companies. The battalions and companies within each league will each be attached with numbers in order, such as the First Battalion, the Second Battalion, the First Company, and the Second Company. Each league will set up a commander above the battalions and companies, referred to as the Commander of the Mongolian Banner Security Force of the Ulanqab League and the Commander of the Mongolian Banner Security Force of the Ih Ju League, with the league heads concurrently serving as commanders. 4) System: The battalion commanders of each banner or the company commanders concurrently held by the princes are directly subordinate to the commander of the security force of their respective league. The company commanders within each battalion are directly subordinate to their battalion commander, and the platoon leaders within each company are directly subordinate to their company commander, following a layer-by-layer control. The commanders of the security forces of each league are directly subordinate to the Suiyuan Region Garrison Commander. Their subordinate units, regarding organization, education, and the deployment of troops, are under the command and control of the garrison commander. However, regarding their internal affairs, such as financial management, sanitation, personnel transfers, supplements, and the temporary deployment of troops for bandit suppression within each banner, they can handle them on one hand and report to the garrison commander on the other. 5) Uniforms: Uniforms are uniformly gray, prepared by the garrison headquarters, deducted from salaries, or made by themselves according to the style. 6) Firearms and Ammunition: First, each banner will be ordered to report the number and type of firearms and ammunition. Those with damaged firearms will be requested by the garrison headquarters to the commander-in-chief for replenishment. Ammunition will also be requested by the garrison headquarters for replenishment when necessary. 7) Salaries: Salaries will be handled according to the regulations in the salary table. However, the circumstances of each banner are different and can be increased or decreased appropriately according to the conditions of their respective banners, but they must be reported to the garrison headquarters at any time. 8) Training: In addition to each team making every effort to find military personnel who are proficient in both Han and Mongolian languages to serve as officers for training, each banner will select one official to study in the troops and agencies designated by the garrison headquarters. Upon completion, they will return to their banner to reorganize and train. 9) Flags and Armbands: The flags will be red and white side by side, with the Blue Sky with a White Sun emblem attached to the top. The size will imitate the flags used by the army, with the team number written on it, such as the Nth Battalion or Nth Company of the Mongolian Banner Security Force of a certain league. The armbands will be white with a red border, with the Blue Sky with a White Sun attached to the center, with the soldier's name and the number of the platoon in his company, and the number of the banner and team, all indicated in both Han and Mongolian languages. 10) Communication: Communication between Han and Mongolian troops is extremely important when cooperating in bandit suppression. In addition to temporarily stipulating identification flags and identification badges for communication, each Mongolian Banner Security Force must send buglers to designated agencies to learn the communication code. In addition to officers, each team must have at least two or three Mongolian soldiers who can speak Chinese for communication. 11) If there are any omissions or amendments to this outline, they may be amended at any time and reported to the Commander-in-Chief for record. 12) This outline will be implemented from the date it is submitted for approval (March 10).

The Shantou Radio Station Begins Operation 62

A dispatch from Shantou reports that the Ministry of Communications sent Shi Zhongyang to Shantou to establish a shortwave radio station. The site was selected at No. 1-3, Zhenping Road, last month. Today (the 11th), it began receiving and sending telegrams from various locations. The set telegram rates are: 1) Chinese plain text, within the province or to another province, is 10 cents per word. 2) Chinese code text is 20 cents per word. 3) Foreign plain text is 20 cents per word. 4) Urgent telegrams are charged three times the normal rate. 5) Official and military telegrams are charged half price. 6) Press telegrams, for those who have registered, are charged one-fourth of the normal rate (i.e., 2.5 cents). 7) Hong Kong telegrams are calculated at double the domestic rate. 8) Corrected telegrams are charged one-half more than normal telegrams. 9) Receipt telegrams are charged three words extra. 10) Prepaid reply telegrams, the number of words and grade are determined by the sender. For all of the above official, military, and commercial telegram fees, no accounts will be settled except for prepaid telegram fees. The locations to which the radio station can currently send telegrams are Shanghai, Nanjing, Ningbo, Anqing, Wuhu, Chengdu, Hankou, Guangzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Beiping, Tianjin, Jinan, Shenyang, Chongqing, Wanxian, Kunming, Nanchang, Kanmen, Qingdao, Tunxi, Shengshan, Yichang, Chongming, Changsha, Dinghai, Hong Kong, etc. (11th)

The Coronation and Military Review of the King of Siam 63

A dispatch from Shantou reports that the King of Siam, Rama VII, held his coronation ceremony on the 25th of last month. From the 24th onwards, the entire city had a three-day holiday. Chinese stores and schools were also ordered to close. A friend returned from Siam and described the recent grand occasion in Bangkok. According to him, the King of Siam went to Ratchasima on March 1st to inspect the field exercises of the Second Division. On that day, at dawn, he departed via the northern route by car. In the afternoon, he arrived at Ratchasima. On the 2nd, he inspected various barracks and reviewed the night exercises of the Third Division in the evening. On the 3rd, he reviewed the combined exercises of the Fourth Division on horseback. In the afternoon, he inspected the administrative agencies in various locations in Korat and participated in the opening ceremony of the Lam Takhong River. On the 4th, he departed by car in the morning and transferred to a carriage to review the combat exercises of the Third Division. The grand occasion was unprecedented in the country. News reporters and film experts from various countries all followed to take photos. Unfortunately, the Chinese news media did not pay much attention. Since King Rama VII is working hard to strengthen the country, his military preparations are worthy of attention. His scheduled itinerary included: inspecting the combat exercises of the Fourth Division on the morning of the 5th; visiting Wat Pa Nom Wan Temple on the 6th; reviewing the field exercises of the Second Division on the 7th, 8th, and 9th; returning south to Kong to inspect the installation of train tracks on the 10th; visiting the airfield on the 11th to review air force flights and test the new tactics of aerial bombing; reviewing all army drills in the afternoon and holding a banquet in the evening; and returning to Bangkok from Ratchasima Province on the 12th. The friend left Siam on the 4th and arrived in Shantou early this morning. (March 11th)

Establishment of Petition Boxes in Various Counties of Liaoning Province 64

A dispatch from Shenyang reports that Chen Wenxue, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, proposed at an administrative conference held with the county magistrates at the end of last year that petition boxes be set up in the street markets of each county to allow people to freely report issues and promote freedom of speech. Tian Qinglan, the magistrate of Zhangwu County, also proposed a plan to install petition boxes for the public. A resolution was passed, and the Department of Civil Affairs drafted the scope and rules for submission, which were then circulated for compliance. Now, the Department of Civil Affairs, considering that both the petition boxes proposed by the department and the petition boxes for the public proposed by the magistrate of Zhangwu County are intended to allow people to express their opinions and broaden avenues for speech, has decided to cancel the name "petition boxes" and uniformly name them "petition boxes" to match the reality. It has also drafted twelve rules for the petition boxes, which have been submitted to the provincial government for approval and circulated to the counties for compliance, to seek understanding of public grievances. The rules are as follows: 1) The public is allowed to submit written petitions at any time to report local tyrants, evil gentry, bandits, corrupt officials who harm the local community, for investigation and handling. 2) The public is allowed to submit written petitions at any time to suggest matters that should be developed or reformed in county administration, for adoption. 3) The submitted petitions must include the real name and address of the submitter and be accompanied by a guarantee to be valid. 4) The petitions do not have to follow a specific format, but the words must be clear and easy to understand. 5) The county magistrate must carefully investigate and handle the defendants and the matters stated in the petitions. The defendants must not be arrested or imprisoned without solid evidence. 6) The county magistrate must strictly keep the name of the submitter confidential, but if the reported matters are found to be maliciously false accusations, the case may be summoned for verification and punishment. 7) The petition box is located outside the county government gate, in a place convenient for the public to access. 8) The box is made of wood, and the size is determined by each county itself, but it must have a flat hole on top and a door on the side for opening and submission. 9) The box door is locked, and the key is kept by the county magistrate. 10) The county magistrate must personally open the box once a day and immediately investigate and handle any submitted petitions. 11) These rules must be written on a wooden sign and hung on the side of the box for public awareness. 12) These rules will be implemented from the date of promulgation. (March 10)

Special Salt Fields Discovered in Lushun 65

Most Suitable for Industrial Soda

World News Agency reports that Professor Fanze Tsuneya of the Lushun Japanese Institute of Technology is currently engaged in research on industrial soda. He says that a few years ago, he accidentally discovered that a part of the salt fields in Lushun-Dalian is different from ordinary salt fields, with a reddish color. After research, it was determined that its concentration is quite high. The salt content of ordinary salt fields is on average 78%, while this salt field exceeds 95%. It is most excellent for industrial soda, which is a raw material for glass manufacturing. He has been researching for two years as to why this special salt field was formed and has recently discovered the reason: it is due to the burial of shellfish and algae in the ground, which decomposes and promotes the crystallization of this higher concentration. This special salt field is indeed very complete for industrial soda and is more economical than conventional soda. Various glass companies have placed orders. However, the production area is limited to a part of the Lushun salt fields, and the annual production is only 4,000 to 5,000 tons, which will be exhausted in a few years. With the help of the Kwantung Government, test salt fields have been set up in both the Goto and Lushun areas, with the aim of producing the same salt as the special salt fields. After repeated research, it is known that although the special salt fields in Lushun are a natural process, the same salt can be expected to be produced artificially. The results of the tests at the end of August last year will soon be revealed, and success is expected. Local news.

Wuxi 67

Personnel Sent to Wuxi for Silk Exhibition: The National Goods Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government, in order to hold a national silk exhibition, sent Tang Qi, the Chief of the General Affairs Section of the hall, to Wuxi a few days ago to contact and collect items. They also hired five local gentlemen, Chen Zhanru, Cheng Bingruo, Qian Fenghao, Li Zhong, and Wu Bangjie, as special collection commissioners for the county, who began collecting items immediately. Yesterday, Section Chief Tang took the Taihu Wheel to Wuxing and then transferred to Suzhou, Danyang, and other counties to collect items.

Reorganization of the Municipal Office: The Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office of the Municipal Commission has been established for eight months since its establishment last autumn. The preparatory period has long expired. Now, an electric order was received from the Department of Civil Affairs stating that since the Municipal Organization Law has not yet been promulgated, the originally established Municipal Preparatory Office should be concluded and stopped. On the other hand, seven to nine people with rich experience and good reputation in the local area should be selected to organize a municipal committee to be responsible for handling municipal affairs. Director Sun believes that the organization of the municipal committee is extremely important and specially proposed the 33rd office meeting. It was decided that the Municipal Preparatory Office would be uniformly concluded by the end of March. The Municipal Office is now preparing for the handover. Yesterday afternoon, the Municipal Committee held its fourth meeting at the Municipal Office to discuss how to organize the municipal committee in accordance with the order of the department. After discussion, it was decided to submit a report to the provincial department for review.

A Large Number of Refugees Arrive at Bashi Bridge Again: Bashi Bridge Town, a town under the jurisdiction of the county, suddenly received more than 40 refugee boats from Jiangbei at 10 a.m. yesterday, with five to six hundred male and female refugees led by Gu Yonggu, selling smuggled salt to the people in the nearby villages. In the evening, the 12th sub-bureau of the town's public security sent police and the chamber of commerce to suppress them. The refugees then left the town and went towards Dongfang Bridge.

Changzhou 68

North Township Bandits Shoot Two People: The remaining associates of Wan Gou Da Bao and Lao Hu, bandit leaders already executed in the north township of Wu Yi, have been secretly active recently, plotting revenge. They intended to kill workers at the Fourth District Public Office. On the afternoon of the 22nd, Lu Kuang, an assistant at the office, accompanied by five members of the Longhutang police squad, armed and in tow, planned to go to his home in Xiaoxinqiao. On the way, while passing through the Chashiqiao area, they suddenly discovered five bandits. They first shined a flashlight at them, and then opened fire. The police squad returned fire. Fortunately, Lu Kuang hid behind them. Bandit bullets hit passersby Fan Guiqing in his left and dark big toes. Fan was hit by four bullets in his right leg and three in his left. The left one then attempted to escape by wading across the river. He was further injured in the water and may be in mortal danger.

Committee Members from the Ministry of Judicial Administration Leave Changzhou: The Ministry of Judicial Administration ordered Section Chief Zhang Yuhai and staff member Wang Qufei to come to Changzhou to investigate the situation after the establishment of the county court. On the morning of the 22nd, they went to investigate the internal workings of the court. They then went to the local prison and detention center to investigate. They were quite satisfied with the work of the prisoners. In the afternoon, they visited the eastern suburbs and then took the train back to Beijing at around 5 p.m. to report on their mission.

Page 10

Bandits Rampant in the Eastern Township: Bandits have recently been openly active in the Yu Dong, Yu Xi, and San Yi districts of the eastern township, burning, looting, and killing with great ferocity. On the night of the 21st, a group of bandits suddenly attacked the Gongsi, Zhongba, and Siyangba areas, seizing all the firearms, over two hundred pieces, from the third squad of the county police team and the militia of the industrial team. They also kidnapped many people from Nanfu. Squad leader Xu Guanxiong fled back to Tongcheng on the 22nd. The situation is serious due to this incident. The provincial police squad's machine gun team rushed back to suppress them. The special police team stationed at the gate and the merchant corps in the city are blocking the routes. The naval fleet stationed at the Lujing Port took the defense of Tongcheng seriously. Under the command of the Yingrui warship captain Lin Yuanquan, a landing party of naval infantry was stationed in vacant rooms of the General Chamber of Commerce to take charge of security. A temporary curfew has been declared throughout the county. The County Court Thoroughly Investigates the Opium Trafficking Case: The Nantong County Court has recently discovered that opium dens are numerous within its jurisdiction, with private sales and trafficking rampant. A large amount of opium is imported and sold daily to Taixing, Rugao and other counties. There are also cases of bribery of government officials to allow passage. President Dong and Prosecutor Zhu are thoroughly investigating the matter and have issued a notice allowing people to report such cases.

Meeting on Vehicle Requisition Case: Party and government personnel from the three counties of Nantong, Rugao, and Haimen met in Tongcheng on the 22nd to discuss the case of military and police requisitioning of vehicles for bandit suppression. A method was agreed upon and handed over to the military and police organs for implementation.

Zhenjiang 69

Zhenjiang Police and Doctor's Guild Holds Inaugural Meeting: The Zhenjiang Doctor's Guild has been actively working to prepare for its establishment and held its inaugural meeting yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m. at the Provincial Medical Hospital.

Suzhou Boy Scouts Prepare to Participate in Review: The Jiangsu Provincial Boy Scouts have already organized a preparatory committee in Zhenjiang to prepare everything for participating in the First National General Review. They have been working on various aspects in recent days.

He is scheduled to depart tomorrow.

Jiangyin 70

Commercial Reorganization Association Submits Petition to the Province for Explanation: The county government, acting on orders to abolish local commercial and civil coordination associations, immediately instructed the association to comply and ordered the county chamber of commerce to take over. It is learned that the Commercial Reorganization Association believes that the county chamber of commerce has not legally organized according to the Law on Industrial and Commercial Guilds, and has specially submitted petitions to the Provincial Commercial Reorganization Association and the county party headquarters, respectively, to request instructions.

Thorough Investigation of Grain Donation and Release: Rice merchant Chen Jingui, entrusted by Nantong Dada Company and others, purchased 1,000 shi of white rice from Wuxi in the name of providing relief to the people. 500 shi passed through Jiangyin, and had already passed Huangtiangang Port. Due to the bill of lading, it was detained by the county, and the Public Security Bureau and the Chamber of Commerce were ordered to investigate. Regarding the donation issue, the county government also ordered the Public Security Bureau to thoroughly investigate. Chen Jingui's passport was issued by Nantong County on February 16th, stating 500 shi. The freight note was issued by Wuxi Chang Yutai on March 10th, totaling 200 shi of white yuan rice at 14 yuan, 1 jiao and 4 fen per shi, and 80 shi of white geng rice at 14 yuan, 7 jiao and 6 fen per shi, totaling 4,687 yuan. There was also a tax ticket from the Wuxi Huangbudun Tax Office, totaling 180 shi of white geng rice, with a total tax of 9 yuan. The General Bureau ordered the North Outer Branch Bureau to investigate and handle the matter yesterday. The Pingbao reported on the 22nd that the matter of detaining grain and releasing it after donation was ordered to be thoroughly investigated by the Public Security Bureau to see if there was any extortion. It should not be difficult to get to the bottom of this. According to insiders, this rice was indeed trafficked by Pan Jintai, and Chen Jingui is Pan's brother-in-law. Pan is the leader of the net boat gang and has repeatedly used passports to traffic rice overseas, often exporting from Changshu or Xutang. Now, due to other obstacles, he is taking the route through Huangtiangang Port to Nantong, and then transferring it to Ningbo fishing boats for overseas export. The matter of paying donations when passing through Huang Nan Port this time is unknown, but the black money used has indeed reached several hundred yuan. The tax is handled by rice brokers Wu A Quan, Sheng Xiaofeng, and Wang Shirong. However, since it is claimed to be providing relief to the people, why is it necessary to privately pay black money? This is also a question worth studying. According to the above records, the rice merchants paid dock donations, which is not without reason.

Yangzhou 71

Procuring Saigon Rice for Famine Relief: The harvest in our county last winter was very poor, and the spring famine this year is even more severe, causing the risk of starvation in various villages. It is heard that a large amount of Saigon rice has arrived in Shanghai. The county government and the Chamber of Commerce have already taken measures to purchase some through the Jianghai Customs to set up a bureau for price controls. It is heard that the Daqiaoshi Chamber of Commerce is also purchasing 3,000 shi in the same way, transporting it to the city six times from the Yangtze River to provide relief.

Zhenqing Salt Shao Boat Robbery Case: The Zai Shengchang boat, which travels between Zhenjiang and Qingjiang, left Zhenjiang with the Run Tong and Gui boats on the evening of the 21st. After boarding passengers, it arrived in Yangzhou at around 1 a.m. on the 22nd. It sailed to Wutaishan and suddenly encountered a bandit boat carrying more than ten bandits. They opened fire and ordered the boat to stop, boarded the boat, and searched and robbed passengers of their clothing, foreign jewelry, and belongings. They then returned to their small boat and left. The robbed Run Tong and Gui boats are still parked at the scene of the incident, and the county government has been notified to investigate. It is also learned that the Dada Yanshao class Yang boat, towing the Flying Eagle boat, was traveling from Yan to Shao the day before when it reached the Qiushuge area in Lvze Lake, 30 li from Shao. Dozens of bandits, riding in small boats, swarmed aboard, robbing over a thousand yuan in cash. Male and female passengers were all searched, and foreign jewelry was looted. Even the crotches of the female passengers were searched. Residents on both banks heard the alarm and beat gongs, but the bandits had already looted to their hearts' content and left.

Shaobozhen Rice Shop Robbed: At 1 a.m. on the 21st, eight bandits, holding sunflower wooden sticks, dug a hole and crowded into the Yang Guangtai rice shop on Shaobozhen Street. Speaking with a Yanfu accent, they demanded 400 yuan in cash from the owner. There were no men in the shop, so the women knelt down and begged. The bandits searched and looted all the clothing and jewelry, opened the main door, and left.

Gaoyou 72

A family of eight relied solely on the meager income from over ten mu of ancestral land for their livelihood. Due to the famine last year, they harvested nothing. In addition, rice and firewood have become increasingly expensive recently, making their daily diet even more difficult. The other day, they pawned their worn-out cotton robe for over two thousand wen to buy several sheng of rice in Jieshou. Because they were short two copper coins, the rice shop refused to give them the rice. Zhang returned home in anger, bought several jin of flour and a package of arsenic, mixed it into the flour, and told his family to make cakes to fill their hunger. After the whole family ate, they died one after another. It is truly tragic.

Rice Prices Rising Daily: Rice prices in the county are rising daily because the rice mills have little inventory and lack sources. Top-quality rice is 21 yuan per dan, medium-quality rice is 20 yuan and 4 jiao, and low-quality rice is 20 yuan. It is said that there is still a tendency to see higher prices.

Qingjiang 73

Recent Disturbances at Two Provincial Schools: It is heard that Wang Zhongqi, the principal of Huai'an Middle School, has resigned and been approved. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education appointed Chen Shishen to take over, but the teachers and students of the entire school were dissatisfied and went on strike on the 15th. It is learned that Chen formally took over on the 18th, and former principal Wang also plans to leave. However, the school has not yet resumed classes, although the director of studies, Xia Yi, is doing his best to maintain order and prepare to resume classes today (20th), but to no avail. In addition, seven of the school's former teachers, Wu Fuzhi (drawing), Su Youzhang (English), Zeng Pinren, Tang Weizhou (both Chinese), Hang Haichuan (history and geography), Hua Rucheng (biology), and Xu Gongwei (mathematics and physics), have also expressed their intention to leave with former principal Wang. It is difficult to predict how this will be resolved in the future. In addition, at Huaiyin Agricultural School, students previously opposed the make-up examinations for the winter vacation. Provincial supervisor Cao Shutian telegraphed the department for instructions and received a reply ordering the expulsion of the striking students. If all the students strike, they will all be expelled. If there is any resistance, the local authorities will be asked to assist. Upon receiving this news, the students of the school obeyed the department's orders and took the examinations as scheduled. The disturbance was safely resolved.

New Names Selected for Siyang City Gates: Siyang County Magistrate Ha Fusheng previously announced a solicitation for names for the four city gates. The solicitation period ended on the 15th. The county government convened various agencies to publicly select names, with the name with the most identical entries being considered suitable. It is calculated that on that day, more than ten people who submitted entries were inspected, and more than forty votes were cast. As a result, Gu Daoxuan's proposed name (Pointing to the Sun) for the east gate was considered suitable, Chen Shengru's proposed name (Mirror Lake) for the south gate was considered suitable, and Ni Yangke's proposed names (Peach Garden) and (Approaching the Canal) for the west gate and north gate were considered suitable.

Rugao 74

Continued Report on the Arrest of Wei Zhanbei and Others: It is learned that after the arrest of Ji Zhanbei, a former executive committee member of the county, Xue Chengzong, the current alternate executive committee member, Chen Dufu, Zhong Jieyuan, Liu Heqing, and Zhou Wu, the six people were interrogated yesterday by Shen Cheng. The court sentenced Ji Zhanbei to the Jiangsu Higher Court, Xue Chengzong and others were each fined 60 yuan, and each paid a 200 yuan shop guarantee. A Kidnapping Case Occurs in the Hedong Township: The Jiang surname owner of a pharmacy in the Hedong Township of the northwest township of Rugao City was kidnapped on the night of the 19th by eight or nine bandits, wielding wooden-cased guns, who broke down the door.

The Remaining Bandits of the Pan Gang are Rampant: Fisherman Li of the Piancha Dongyang Port fled back from the bandit den yesterday. According to him, after the bandits of the Pan Gang were suppressed, the remaining members of the Xue Shen Guan Xi joined forces with Yuan Zhaorui, gathering more than 500 people with more than 40 boats, over 200 rifles, many box cannons, six handheld machine guns, and six or seven steel and bronze cannons. They rob cargo ships at sea, and buy local thugs to act as spies, land to kidnap people, and if the ransom is not paid for a long time, the men are forced into labor, the women are raped, or they are shot. Their daily necessities are purchased by local thugs, and bullets and other items are delivered by Ningbo sand boats.

Several pirate ships suddenly arrived, and dozens of pirates landed with weapons. They kidnapped five carpenters who were repairing ships in the dock at the Da'an Tou: Huang Ming'er, Huang Sheng'er, Ge Er, Wu Da, and Yang Da.

Jiashan 75

Kidnapping Cases Appear Frequently: Four uninvited guests suddenly arrived at the Gu Aisheng home in Dingzhaibei last night, armed with box cannons, and forced them to offer silver. Failing to do so, they kidnapped Gu's younger brother, Longsheng, and demanded a ransom of 2,000 yuan within ten days. At that time, a gong sounded nearby, and the bandits fired a shot while escorting the hostage, injuring Ah Liu, who was rowing a rice boat on the river, as an innocent victim.

The Ma Lan Society Performs: In the Jinming Village area of Xitang, the Ma Lan Society idol, four statues, perform on the 22nd of February every year with ceremonial guards. This year, they performed again. It is truly unbelievable that this action took place during a period when bandits are rampant.

Jiashan 76

The Origin of the Rumor of Another Robbery in Luxu: At 3 p.m. on the 22nd, it was rumored in Luxu Town, Wu that it had been robbed again by lake bandits. A detailed investigation revealed that it was the steamer from Luli to Jiashan that saw the security corps at Lu Nan Gate that day sounding the whistle to gather, armed with real bullets, and leaving South Gate. After the boat traveled a mile, the sound of gunfire was very intense, closely resembling both sides opening fire. The sound lasted longer and further north, so it was speculated that the bandits were robbing Luxu. However, after inquiring to Xiazhen Temple, there was no definite news. In addition, Luxu has no telephone communication. Therefore, the steamer from Jiashan to Luxu only went as far as Xiazhen Temple. News was silent and could not be explored.

The Release of Hostages in the Yangjiabin Robbery Case: In the Yangjiabin robbery case, fourteen hostages were kidnapped, and four quick-firing rifles were robbed. It is learned that the bandits clashed with the Suzhou Water Police team near Zhujing Liujiang the other day, seizing more than twenty quick-firing rifles and one small steel cannon. They then retreated to the Henggang East area to rest and celebrate, claiming that the quick-firing rifles robbed in Yangjiabin were of great profit. They ordered that all fourteen hostages be redeemed and sent back. However, four hostages were taken by a smaller gang and are near Fengjing, so they have not yet returned. The ten hostages were each treated to wine and food and were safely released. The above news was told by the returned hostages. Qidun Kidnapping Case: Chen Muguan of Xitang Qidun was kidnapped by bandits last night, tortured with a cangue, and agreed to pay 250 yuan for his life. The bandits agreed and received the money on the spot, leaving in an easterly direction.

Xiaoshan 77

Thorough Investigation of the Quota Donation Bureau Director's Embezzlement: One tenth of the quota donation item of the Shaoshan bamboo curtain area has been implemented to fund disaster relief. However, since the collection, very few have complied with the order to report and remit to the provincial treasury. The Department of Finance specially dispatched inspector Shen Jiwei to Shaoxing to investigate. If former Director Feng is found to have committed fraud, he must be severely punished.

Hangyong Railway to be Connected in Two Phases: The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway is over 1,000 li long. Currently, only the section from Shanghai to Hangzhou is open to traffic. The small section from Cao'e to Ningbo has also been built. However, the section from Hangzhou to Cao'e has not yet been constructed. The Ministry of Railways has recently planned construction. The Hangyong connection will be carried out in two phases. The first phase is from the Hangzhou Xian crossing to Xiaoshan Xixing, and the second phase is from Xixing to Cao'e. The total cost is estimated to be over 4 million yuan. This fund will be paid from the Boxer Indemnity.

Education News Highlights

Ministry of Education Strictly Orders Jinling and Shanghai Universities to Stop Religious Departments 78

The Ministry of Education instructed the education bureaus of Nanjing and Shanghai special cities: "It has been repeatedly ordered that private schools established by religious organizations must not make religious subjects compulsory and must not conduct religious propaganda on campus. It has recently been discovered that the 'Overview of Arts and Sciences of Jinling University' (1928-1929) published by private Jinling University still has a Department of Religion, and the 'List of Shanghai University' (1929-1930) published by private Shanghai University still has a Department of Religion and Theology, which is inconsistent with the law. The bureau should thoroughly and accurately investigate whether the school still has the aforementioned departments or makes religious subjects compulsory, and order it to stop immediately. If they refuse to comply, the bureau will report to the ministry for handling in accordance with Article 6 of the Regulations on Private Schools." (Note: Article 6 states that when a private school is poorly managed or violates the law, the competent educational administrative agency may revoke its registration or dissolve it.)

Huang Jianzhong Goes to Hubei to Take Office as Director of Education 79

Huang Jianzhong, the newly appointed member of the Hubei Provincial Government and Director of the Department of Education, left Xiaguan by boat on the morning of the 22nd to take office in Hubei. The position of permanent deputy minister left by the Ministry of Education has been approved by the State Council and will be concurrently held by the Director of the Department of General Education of the Ministry of Education. It is said that the Ministry of Education is currently looking for a Director of Higher Education, but no decision has been made yet.

The Training and Supervision Department will Send Personnel to Review Military Education in High Schools 83

The Ministry of Education, in order to have the Training and Supervision Department send personnel to Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in early April to review military education in schools above the high school level, specially issued an order to the education departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, the two special municipal education bureaus, and national universities to comply. The order is as follows: "It is approved that the Training and Supervision Department has sent a memorandum stating that the Ministry has implemented military education in schools above the high school level for more than a year, and the implementation area has spread to 114 schools in 11 provinces, with 99 instructors dispatched. In order to assess the performance of each school in accordance with regulations, it is planned to send personnel to conduct reviews in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in early April. In addition to listing the review districts separately, Cheng Bingren, a lieutenant colonel staff member of the National Military Education Division of the Ministry, is appointed as the review officer for the first district, and Wang Zemin, a lieutenant colonel staff member of the division, is appointed as the review officer for the second district. It is approved that the original documents should be copied and sent to the (Department) (Bureau) (School) for notification and to instruct subordinates to be notified. This order includes one copy of the original district list. The first district includes all national high schools and above in Jiangsu Province (totaling 20 schools) and the private Jinling Middle School. The second district includes the National Central Jiaotong University, the Nanyang High School of Commerce, the Tongji University, the private Jinling University, the Datong University, Zhejiang University, and the provincial and municipal private high schools, totaling 16 schools.

Shanghai County Branch of the Local Education Research Association Held a Discussion Meeting Yesterday 84

The Shanghai County Branch of the Jiangsu Provincial Local Education Research Committee held a discussion meeting at the Suzhou Education Bureau yesterday morning. Training Methods for Each Team 94

Track and field events are individual activities. Athletes are only notified to practice on their own. Men's basketball and volleyball players will concentrate on training at Nányáng High School of Commerce in Shanghai. A football team will definitely not be sent. Women's tennis and basketball players will concentrate on training at Sūzhōu Women's High School. Women's volleyball will be at Jìngzhì Girls' School.

(6) Jiangsu Representative Regulations

1. The selection of track and field athletes shall be determined by the Jiangsu Provincial Sports Games Preparatory Committee.

2. In principle, the championship team shall represent the province in ball games, but outstanding talents from other teams may be dispatched by the Preparatory Committee at its discretion.

3. The Preparatory Committee shall hire a number of staff members to be responsible for management and guidance of each sport.

4. All actions of athletes after arriving in Hángzhōu (such as morning exercises, night rest, accommodation, and diet) must be subject to the instructions of the team leader and must not be violated. Athletes who do not travel with the group must also be subject to the instructions of the staff members of this committee after arriving in Hángzhōu.

5. Travel expenses for athletes dispatched to Hángzhōu shall be provided by the committee (accommodation and meals in Hángzhōu shall be provided by the National Games). Travel expenses for those who do not travel with the group shall be borne by the athletes themselves, unless approved by the committee due to special circumstances.

6. The committee shall not be responsible for the financial expenses of personnel attending the meeting other than the athletes selected by the committee.

7. The uniforms of the selected representatives shall be made by the committee.

8. If an athlete engages in misconduct during the National Games, the committee may impose appropriate penalties or revoke their qualifications.

9. Bring your own luggage and necessary items.

Detailed Report of the Second Day 97

The opening of the Huázhōng Games on the morning of the 19th, as well as the results of various track and field events, were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. The following is a record of the afternoon events of the conference on the 19th. The afternoon of the 19th was entirely devoted to ball games. The situation is as follows:

Tennis: Hàn vs. Wǎn: Hàn Wins

In the morning, only two singles matches were played between Hàn and Wǎn. Wǎn and Hàn each won one match, so the finals were held in the afternoon. As a result, Hàn won. Only one doubles match was played between Hàn and Wǎn in tennis. The result of the afternoon game was also a win for Hàn.

Basketball: Hàn vs. Xiāng (Men): Hàn Wins; Gàn vs. Wǎn (Women): Wǎn Wins

As a result of the men's and women's basketball games between Hàn and Xiāng, Hàn won. In the women's basketball game between Gàn and Wǎn, Wǎn was already at a disadvantage in the first half. The representatives of Wǎn province were Wǎn No. 2 Girls' Middle School, which is the most capable team among the women's basketball teams in Wǎn province. In the second half, the Wǎn team tried its best to compete and managed to turn defeat into victory. The result was a score of 20 to 14, and Wǎn won. The Wǎn team's passing was quick, scoring two consecutive goals in one minute. No wonder the applause was thunderous. The finals will be held with Xiāng in the next few days. The victory in the future is still unknown, but the Wǎn team is indeed confident.

Volleyball: Xiāng vs. È (Women): Xiāng Wins; Gàn vs. È (Men): Gàn Wins

In the women's volleyball game between Xiāng and È, the result was 2-0, and Xiāng won. In the women's volleyball game between Gàn and È, Gàn won.

Football: Xiāng vs. È (Men): È Wins

In the soccer match between Xiāng and È, È won with a score of 4-0.

Swimming Postponed

The swimming preliminaries were originally scheduled to be held at 3:00 p.m. on the 19th, but due to insufficient water in the swimming pool, it will not be available until the afternoon of the 20th. Therefore, there was no swimming competition on the afternoon of the 19th.

Total Scores for Two Days

The total scores for the track and field competitions on the 18th and 19th are calculated as follows: Xiāng men: 63.2 points; women: 12 points. Gàn men: 38.3 points; women: 0 points. È men: 25 points; women: 10 points. Wǎn men: 16.2 points; women: 11 points. Hàn men: 0.2 points; women: did not participate.

Supplementary Record of Results

The women's eight-pound shot put, held on the morning of the 18th, did not have its results available at the time. The following is the supplement. The names have already been detailed in yesterday's draft and will not be recorded again. Women's 8-pound shot put final: 7.27 meters.

Detailed Report of the Third Day 98

The 20th was the third day of the Huázhōng Games. On this day, the weather was clear and refreshing, and the spring breeze was warm. There were more spectators than yesterday, about 20,000 or more. The morning was for track and field events and the men's and women's tennis matches between Xiāng and Gàn. The afternoon was entirely for ball games. The following is a record of the situation:

Swimming Rescheduled Again

The swimming event was originally scheduled to be held on the afternoon of the 19th, but was changed to this afternoon due to the swimming pool not being filled with water. However, the water was still not full today and has been changed to the morning of the 21st. Because the pool is newly built, it has a very strong water absorption capacity. It takes a long time and consumes a lot of energy to pump water with a hand-cranked water pump. It is expected that it will be available tomorrow.

Track and Field Results

The results of the track and field finals on the morning of the 20th are recorded below: Javelin Final: Hé Yìnhuán (Xiāng), Yáng Fāng (Xiāng), Zhào Rùnjí (Xiāng), Huáng Wényì (È), 41.8 meters.

Detailed Report of the Fourth Day 99

Today (21st) is the fourth day after the opening of the Huázhōng Games. It was drizzling last night, and those who like to watch sports events were quite worried that it would rain today. Fortunately, the weather was beautiful, and the sun shone brightly this morning. The event was not diminished because of this, and the weather was warmer than yesterday, which made it more suitable for swimming. First, I will record the opening situation this morning:

Track and Field Completed

The track and field competition was completed yesterday afternoon (20th). At this time, the conference separated the all-around sports from track and field as two championships. Therefore, the scores for the all-around sports should not be included in the track and field competition. As a result of the track and field competition, the scores of each province's men and women and their rankings should be as follows:

Men: Xiāng first, 87

Third, 45.3 points; Wǎn fourth, 18.2 points; Hàn fifth, 2 points.

Women: Xiāng first, 27.5 points; È second, 20 points; Wǎn third, 18.5 points; Gàn fourth, 0 points; Hàn did not participate.

Conference Situation

The sports began at 9:00 a.m. There were fewer spectators in the morning, but no less than 5,000. The tennis final took a long time. It was not finished in the morning and will continue in the afternoon. All-around sports have been completed, and the results are as follows:

Sports Results

1600m relay, 1st Xiāng, 2nd Gàn, 3rd Wǎn, 4th È, time 3 minutes 56.7 seconds. Women's 200m relay, 1st È, 2nd Xiāng, 3rd Wǎn, 4th Gàn, time 31.1 seconds.

Tennis

The men's group was a final between Hàn and Gàn. As a result, Gàn won 3-0. The Gàn players, Huáng Kuíyuán and Lǐ Bìzǔ, were truly experienced veterans with their skilled ball techniques, and they often produced clever shots that were exhilarating.

The women's tennis team consisted of Xiāng versus Wǎn for the final. As a result, Xiāng won 3-0. The Xiāng team had defeated the Gàn team, and they were even more energized by the victory in the war against Wǎn. The Wǎn team was no match for them.

Volleyball

The women's volleyball final was held on the afternoon of the 20th. As a result, Xiāng won. The men's volleyball team was a final between Hàn and Xiāng. The representatives of Xiāng were the Míngdé Middle School team. The Míngdé team was short, lean and capable, and the Hàn team was also very brave. After a long and fierce battle, Xiāng won 2-1.

Basketball

The men's basketball final between È and Hàn was changed to the morning of the 22nd. On the afternoon of the 21st, only the women's basketball game was played, which was the final between Xiāng and Wǎn. The Xiāng team members were stronger than the Wǎn team. The Wǎn team was the No. 2 Girls' Middle School. Although their ball skills were proficient, they were no match for the Xiāng team in terms of strength. In the end, Xiāng won 17-13.

Football

In the football final between Hàn and Gàn, Gàn won 3-0.

Swimming Results

Starting at 2:00 p.m., swimming competitions were held, including the 100-meter freestyle final, the 50-meter freestyle final, the 100-meter backstroke final, and the 1,500-meter final. The 1,500-meter race was not completed due to the cold weather and was changed to the afternoon of the next day. The other results are as follows:

Record of the First Day Shanxi Sports Meet 104

Opening Ceremony

Tàiyuán, 10th: The Shanxi Provincial Games, which had been in preparation for a long time, officially opened at 9:00 a.m. on the 11th at the Little Five Platforms, where the North China ball game competition was held last year. More than 40 schools participated. The first day was basketball and tennis, which were held in five locations: Little Five Platforms, YMCA, and Fàzhuān, Shāngzhuān, and No. 1 Middle School. The 11th was the track and field preliminaries, and the 12th morning was suspended for half a day due to the death anniversary of the Prime Minister. In the afternoon, the finals were still held at the original site. The venue layout was extremely magnificent, surrounded by railings, and a lecture platform was built in the west. On both sides of the platform, the left was the dressing room for male team members, and the right was the dressing room for female team members. Above the venue, small flags of the Party and the country were hung, and a line was drawn long, fluttering and flying without restriction, looking like a long rainbow in the sky. From 8:00 a.m., the athletes and visitors arrived one after another. By 9:00 a.m., it was already crowded. Shāng Qǐyǔ, chairman of the provincial government, presided over the opening ceremony. After the rituals were completed, the chairman delivered a speech, which roughly stated: "Comrades, students, today the Shanxi Provincial Games are held to serve as a preliminary for participating in the Hángzhōu National Games. You will go to Hángzhōu to compete. The quality of your sports depends on your skills. The most important thing is to abide by the rules. People in other provinces used to say that Shanxi's sports were childish, but that's not necessarily true. From the current point of view, there has been considerable progress in sports and education. As for the relationship between sports and life and the nation, you have done a lot of research on sports, so I won’t go into details. Now I will briefly describe the two points that should be paid attention to: (1) Sports and the country. To know whether a country is strong or not, first look at the health and weakness of its national physique. Those with a strong national physique will be able to do good things. On the contrary, no matter how profound their scientific knowledge or how vast their literary research, there are not many who can succeed. It can be seen that the relationship between sports and the country is not superficial. (2) Sports and hobbies. Various sports should be used to reform the bad habits of the nation, such as the British promotion of tennis and the American popularity of baseball. I hope you will do your best to promote various sports to eliminate all kinds of bad habits of the people of Jìn. The effects of this are even better than the law. It is comparable and even surpasses it," and so on. Then, referee Zhāng Wǔchéng reported the order of the sports events, followed by a parade of all the staff and athletes in the venue for one week, and the ceremony was completed. The competition began, and three planes flew from the northwest and hovered over the venue's airspace, making extremely low flights, tilting and tumbling, fluttering and agile. The sound of the plane engine and the sound of military music echoed each other, which was quite a spectacle. The number of male and female athletes participating was about 500 or more, and the number of students and visitors from various schools reached more than 10,000. The perimeter outside the venue was crowded, and the roots of the southeast and two cities were almost filled. The women's visitors mostly occupied the north of the venue, and there were many of them. Many military, government, and civilian officials also came to the meeting to guide. The results of the competitions in various schools were often quite remarkable. However, in the morning, there was a dispute between Yīshī and Chéngchéng over the issue of scoring, which caused the order to be disrupted and the spirit to be dissipated. This was indeed a fly in the ointment. The results of the preliminary rounds on the 10th are listed separately below:
