A Fleeting Smile 107

— Haike

My wife says the Wang family's sister-in-law from next door says her husband often gets up and walks around in his sleep. In reality, he doesn't even know it himself.

Husband: The poor man. That's the freest he gets all day. I wish I could be like that too.

Old Gentleman: Madam, do you have a son?

Woman: Yes, I have only one son.

Old Gentleman: Does he smoke?

Woman: He has never smoked a single cigarette.

Old Gentleman: That's excellent. There's poison in tobacco; it's best not to smoke. Does he often go to gambling dens or brothels?

Woman: He never leaves the house and goes to sleep early every night.

Old Gentleman: Madam, congratulations! Your son is truly a model youth. How old is he?

Woman: Only one year old.

Housewife (addressing the maid sternly): If you don't do your job properly, I'll hire someone else.

Maid: That would be wonderful. The workload here is too heavy; it should be divided between two people.

Spring News from the Lakeside 108

— Songlu

The spring breeze is warm, willows are green, and flowers are red. West Lake, known nationwide for its beauty, is graced by this natural embellishment, further enhancing its charm. In recent days, people in fine attire throng here, shoulder to shoulder, strolling among the Six Bridges and the Three Temples. They are all tourists from afar who have come to enjoy the spring. As a visitor myself, I will select and report the spring news to the readers.

The National Games, which caused a sensation, are about to open on April 1st. The Provincial Games have been underway for days. The athletes from various schools are full of energy, competing on the Meidong High Bridge. In particular, the female students are most excited and colorful. Entering the venue, those in gray shirts and black skirts account for nearly half the number. One only needs to hear the loudness of their cheering to imagine the intensity of the competition in the arena.

The local opera scene on the lake has been very quiet. This year, the Common Dance Stage has reorganized and strengthened its forces, hiring Xiao San Mazi, Li Donglai, and female performers such as He Yurong, Zhou Wenyan, and Zui Yuejuan. They are staging "The Legend of Flying Dragon" and various "Red Scholar" plays. Their appeal is still quite strong. Every day, the audience attendance is more than fifty or sixty percent. The West Lake Amusement Garden has hired female performers Lü Jinfen and the Three Peonies, staging the new play "Heavenly Rain of Flowers" with Gao Tingzan and others. The audience fills the venue to capacity, extremely crowded.

The lakeside hotels are all located in the New Market, making it inconvenient for tourists traveling to and from the lake by boat and carriage. Recently, someone has proposed opening the Xiling Hotel on the edge of Gushan Island, and preparations are actively underway. It is expected to open sometime in the height of spring. At that time, men and women who come to enjoy the spring can avoid a lot of travel fatigue.

After the closing of the Exposition, the local authorities, wishing to leave a permanent memento, specially built an Exposition Memorial Tower in the heart of the lake. The tower has three stories. Climbing the winding staircase, one can ascend to the top of the tower and see the entire lake. The beautiful scenery is like a painting, sufficient to refresh one's spirit.

Record of the Web-Fingered Village in Spain 109

— Yun Sun

Those of us who toil year after year, using our ten fingers to earn our living, often have a strange idea, regretting that we cannot add another hand, increase the number of fingers, to assist in our daily work. Although it may be a joke, it is also a common human sentiment. Recently, I heard that there is a village in Spain where people with webbed fingers gather, and this must be recorded.

In Spain, there is a small village called Podragón, located in the province of Madrid. It is surrounded by towering mountains and barren scenery. Its seclusion and remoteness are like the Peach Blossom Spring of Jin, with little contact with the outside world. A wide road cannot be found, and even a narrow path is not passable. Those who reside in this village, about fifty households, or more than 150 people, sustain themselves by farming. There is no involvement in industry, commerce, or scholarship. The village produces abundant stone, mostly of inferior quality, which is useless and hinders agricultural work. Therefore, without endless hard work, it is impossible to obtain coarse food and warm clothing. The only unique feature of the villagers is that they all have six fingers on each hand. The residents consider having more fingers to be a virtue, as they can assist in operations.

There was a farmer in the village who once joined the army, but after examining his physical condition, he was rejected because of his extra fingers. He was not satisfied and instead asked for an examination by a medical officer. Because he grew up in a village of web-fingered people, he was accustomed to seeing many fingers. If he happened to be outside the village, he would be surprised by the strangeness of having only five fingers. An old farmer in the village once told people the reason for the webbed fingers, saying that hundreds of years ago, webbed fingers were not common. Later, a man and a woman, both with webbed fingers, married. Their descendants all had webbed fingers. Passed down through generations, to this day, they all have six or seven fingers, without exception.

When Chinese people have extra fingers, they often give them the auspicious name of "Six-Fingered Elder." However, if they are weak, short, and small like a baby's, unable to hold things, they are like useless growths. The fingers of those who grow up in the web-fingered village are the opposite. Their strength is equal to the inherent five fingers. They can work side by side, which is also a rare story. The village has many stones, and farming relies on labor. Much depends on the fingers to assist. Is there a divine number existing among them?

A Record of the Night Banquet and Song at the Huanyun Tower 110

— Deng Chunshu

Last autumn, I moved to Baiyun Stream. The stream is the most scenic in our county, and my residence is the Wang family's villa, also occupying the most scenic spot on Yun Stream. Famous scholars' pavilions surround it, and across the stream are Su Dongpo's Purple Vine Pavilion and Yun Nantian's Ouxiang Pavilion. The ruins still exist. Tang Runzhi's Spring Rain Painting Tower and Shi Ganfu's Yi Garden, with their flowers, trees, pavilions, and terraces, are all within sight. The stream turns east to Tangjiawan, a stream flowing between willow trees lining both banks. Next to it is the Confucius Temple. To the right overlooks the ancient Baiyun Ferry, where two boats are connected to carry pedestrians. This tower was formerly named Huanyun. Below it is the Leyu Water Pavilion. I renamed my hall Siyun Thatched Cottage. Behind it is the Jingmi Xuan. Although the book collection does not reach ten thousand volumes, it is enough for browsing. The resident, Wang Ruilin, is now seventy years old. He lives in the eastern part of the tower. His door is always open, and we often visit each other. He is filled with poetry and books, tranquil and elegant. He is skilled in composing music. He had a splendid youth and is truly a romantic figure. On the day of the Hundred Flowers Festival, he invited friends to drink at the Stream Tower and celebrate his birthday. That day, the drizzle was like cream, and the light clouds were like catkins. Zhao Gongmingxuan, Zhou Junqiyan, and my elder brother Chunxian arrived first. Mingxuan is good at poetry and prose. Chunxian is also skilled in composing and playing the flute. Tang Danran, Ding Qinbao, and Liu Quran arrived next. The later arrivals were Tang Junqilin, Qian Junmingshan, and Wang Junbotao. Qilin has been the director of the Huainan Customs Anti-Smuggling Bureau for two years. He resigned due to bandits and soldiers but was not allowed. He came from Yangzhou yesterday. He presented me with a large-character couplet that reads: "The inkstone field has no bad years; the wine country has a long spring." Hanging it in the Siyun Hall is quite fitting. Mingshan went to the Baijia Bridge in the eastern suburbs, five miles from the city. The gentleman usually wears a yellow Taoist robe and hat, walking alone. One can tell at a glance that he is a recluse. Tonight, he is wearing a purple feather

cloak. He also arrived elegantly. So, the lanterns were lit, and we each examined poems and prose, and viewed paintings and calligraphy. After a few rounds of drinks, we took turns playing music and singing. Quran is proficient in the I Ching and is skilled in poetry and painting. He can also sing songs. He is pure and thin, as if he does not eat human food. He started by singing the song "Picking Up Gold." Qinbao and Ruilin followed. Chunxian played the flute again and then the erhu. Ruilin lightly tapped the sandalwood clappers. We then took turns performing several songs, including "Sweeping Flowers," "Three Drunkards," "Matchmaking," and "Conversation." I love listening to singing, but although I have practiced a few excerpts in small banquets, I am not yet proficient. Qiyan said that the Yuan music of the prosperous age has not been heard for a long time. Mingshan asked about the Gongshang Gongche scales, debating with Quran for a long time, and then he also had some understanding. I said that the Book of Songs was originally ancient ballads, but now they have been lost for a long time. I asked if anyone knew what the Gongshang scale was for the poem "The Yellow River Far Above" on the old flag pavilion painting. No one could answer. Qiyan said that the three chapters of "Pan Huan" were quite similar to the current small songs, so he tried to sing it. Chunxian immediately played the zither to accompany him. Although it was the first time he had played this tune, it was surprisingly in sync. After the meal, the lingering emotions had not subsided. Chunxian sang "Splitting Jade." Ruilin sang "Man Jiang Hong." Qinbao sang several small tunes. Qinbao is seventy-three years old, but his voice is like a beautiful woman's. It is truly a rare and interesting thing. The clock struck twelve. The cold rain was pattering. The guests began to bid farewell. I enjoyed this gathering very much, so I took up my pen and wrote a record of it in the rustling sound of the rain and the blurred shadows of my dreams. I feel that the lingering sound is still in my ears. (No payment accepted)

A Three-Character Cure for Jealousy 111

— Ji Qin

Recently, a friend told me about a certain person in Yushan, who started a business at a young age and had some assets. His wife was talented but jealous, and she could not bear anything. All the maids in the house had to be chosen for their odd ugliness and baldness. At that time, the man was nearing fifty. He was both afraid of Ji Chang and lamented like Bo Dao. He reluctantly agreed to adopt his younger brother's son as his heir. Then, he divided the shops he had created in the past for him to manage, and he did not bother with the income and expenditure of money. However, the adopted son's wife was treacherous and vicious. She actually regarded the divided property as her own and viewed her brother and sister-in-law as superfluous burdens. One day, the man was summoned by a friend and hurriedly went to the capital. He immediately took twenty gold coins from the shop to buy gifts. Unfortunately, the adopted son's wife found out and began to roar and rage. She angrily scolded her husband, saying, "This money belongs to my son. Why give it to this old, childless man?" At that time, the man's wife happened to pass by the window. When she heard these words, she fainted from anger. When she woke up, she cried and refused to eat for three days.

Half a month later, a letter arrived from the capital, informing them that the man had found a job in a certain agency. The wife's heart relaxed slightly. Then, she entrusted matchmakers everywhere to find two girls from poor families, about seventeen or eighteen years old, beautiful and likely to bear sons, and bought them with heavy gold. She took them to the capital. At that time, the man was free from work and was playing chess with a guest. The doorman announced that his wife had arrived, and he was greatly shocked. He abandoned the chess pieces all over the ground and quickly greeted her respectfully. He asked about her intentions. She said that she had come specifically to send him concubines. He did not believe her at all. Before long, he saw the two concubines arrive as well. They were beautiful and charming, making people love them. As a result, he was overjoyed and immediately lived with them in the guest house. The wife ordered them to take turns serving him in bed. Those who were not on duty would stay to accompany her. After several months, they were both pregnant. A year later, they gave birth to two sons. The wife was overjoyed. She then packed her bags and returned home, saying that she was going to collect debts from the adopted son and his wife. She took back all the property and declared that the reason she had found concubines for her husband was for these three words: "(Old, childless man)." The adopted son's wife regretted it too late and eventually died of grief and anger.

Common Sense Gleanings 112

— Tang Bihua

When you meet a friend on the street and ask each other for your addresses, do not speak loudly. Be careful that bad people might hear it and use the address to commit fraud. You must be cautious.

When writing letters to others, except for express mail and registered mail, do not write your address on the envelope. Be careful that others might throw away the envelope, and someone might pick it up, which could easily lead to complications. Also, both parties are easily confused.

When you see an advertisement and want to buy something, it is best to see it first and then buy it. If you live in another city, you can ask a nearby relative or friend to handle it for you, so you won't suffer a loss.

When a person goes to take the train with luggage, it is very inconvenient to buy a ticket. You may as well go to the China Travel Service the day before you travel to buy a ticket in advance. It is much more convenient.

Brief Notes on Orchids and Irises 115

— Diru

Orchids and irises are elegant flowers.) One stem and one flower is an orchid. One stem and several flowers is an iris.) And those with plain hearts are especially rare and valuable. Now the spring breeze is warm, and the people of Shaoxing who sell flowers gather in our Wu. Knowing that those who buy orchids and irises want to get a plain heart, they often make fake ones to deceive people. The orchid flowers that have already bloomed and have plain hearts are treated with sulfur. They light a fire to fumigate them. The gas adheres to the heart of the flower, and the heart turns plain. When they bloom again next year, there will be no plain hearts at all. Buyers try it repeatedly and know that it is fake. Iris flower stamens often have extremely green and plump ones. They tell people that this is a good species and must be a plain heart. This is also a fake to deceive people. According to those who have been doing this for a long time, it is the jade bamboo in the medicine. They pick it and insert it into the iris flower root, exposing an inch or so, to dazzle people. By the time they are bought home and bloom, the flowers are like shepherd's purse flowers. (That is, vegetable flowers.) Buyers are also often deceived. A friend mentioned wanting to buy orchids and irises, so I told him about this and told the readers of the newspaper who have a fondness for orchids and irises.

Warmth on My Heart (154) 116

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 14: Red Flames Soar, Rails Admire the Filial Daughter; Red Carpet Lies Flat, Meeting Famous Actors Instantly. It should be explained that the Mirror Club is directly opposite the racecourse. Its location is very good. It is quite suitable for watching horse racing. So I invited many sisters of the flower world to look at the distance from the railing. In the past, many people were wholeheartedly watching horse racing. Not like now, horse racing has become a specialized gambling machine. The girl named Bi Xiguan is an unrestrained character. She treats Zheng Yanxiu like a little brother. What does it matter if he can't squeeze down and hugs her? Moreover, people who are girls, especially those who are unimportant, insist that there is a kind of rare and strange person in Shanghai, thinking that something strange has happened. They are all looking at the building over there. There is also a group of people who have nothing to do on weekdays wandering around the streets, and they are crowding there to start a riot, clapping and applauding. After this riot, Zheng Yanxiu dared not stand on the balcony again. Bi Xiguan said indifferently, "What are you afraid of them? They eat their fill of white rice and clear water, and they specialize in other people's business. Don't pay attention to them." However, the setting sun is slanting west, and the shadows are scattered. After the skipping, the people watching the horse racing gradually dispersed. There are also many tourists who go to Zhang Yuan. This Zhang Yuan is also known as Wei Chun Yuan. It is pitiful that Shanghai, such a large and prosperous city in China, does not have a public garden for Chinese people to open and walk around. Because in the past, Chinese people lived in the concessions and forgot their origin. It seems that foreigners are the masters in the concessions, and they are guests. Therefore, it has become a situation of reversing the guest and host, and taking over the position of the host, which means the racecourse on the side of Nicheng Bridge. Foreigners can casually run in, but when Chinese people go to the door, they are turned away. In addition, there are several parks in the concession that Chinese people are not allowed to enter. Even the park entrance is hung with a sign that dogs and Chinese people are not allowed to enter, putting Chinese people and dogs in the same category. The dogs they are referring to are naturally not Chinese people's dogs, but Westerners' dogs. Chinese people are not allowed to enter either, not to mention dogs. The prohibition of dogs from entering is because dogs will trample on flowers and trees, or scare children, etc. Why are Chinese people not allowed to enter? This is clearly insulting Chinese people. But at that time, the Chinese people's view was that this place can only be enjoyed by foreigners. Since it is written that Chinese people are not allowed to enter, they had to look and leave. But they don't think that this is a park built by the public, and of course it is for the public to play. Chinese people in the concession pay taxes, and they pay a lot of taxes. As a result, they are regarded as equal to the dogs carried by foreigners. At that time, there were also a few people who understood a little bit, and they argued with the concession authorities, why did Chinese people not enjoy the benefits of the concession park? Later, they delineated a piece of land near the Suzhou River, which was regarded as a park for Chinese people to stroll. But it was a grassy field with a few clumps of trees. There was no equipment at all, and Chinese people did not run to that place.

Financial Weekly: Calm and Quiet Call Loan Market 117

Yesterday, Sunday, the prices for both call loan types were identical in the early market: seven mace, two fen, zero one hao, two hu, and a half for the call price; and three fen for the silver call. Remittance transactions amounted to 340,000 in the early market and 185,000 in the afternoon market. There were no transactions in banknotes in either market. On the same day, over 1.9 million in foreign public bonds were collected and redeemed, and over 2.1 million in silver public bonds were collected and redeemed. Call loan transactions still amounted to over 3.3 million. Banks were closed for the entire day, so all buying, selling, collection, and redemption were suspended. Smaller money shops reported that the early market price for small Jiangnan silver dollars was six mace, one fen, and five li, with no transactions occurring. The afternoon market price was six mace, one fen, and five li and a half, with transactions amounting to 4,000 jiao. Overseas Silver Prices: British Decrease, American Increase 118

Yesterday was Sunday. As usual, customs and all foreign banks, both Chinese and foreign, were closed, so there were no reports on the gold market, foreign exchange, or foreign stocks. However, according to London telegrams, the price of standard silver continued to decrease, with the near-term price decreasing by .0625 to 19 pence and .875. The forward price also decreased by .0625 to 19 pence and .6875. The Bank of China was selling, and silver companies were buying, with flat market conditions. The British pound decreased against the US dollar by .125 to $4.86625, while the US dollar increased against the British pound by .125 to $4.86675. Bond Prices on the Stock Exchange: Sideways Movement with Slight Increase Last Week 119

Readjustment bonds show fatigue . . . Trading volume still reaches over 40 million

Over the past week, the situation in the local bond market has been such that spot transactions are still slow. The total trading volume for the entire week was 134,000 yuan, with readjustment bonds accounting for 68,000 yuan, financial bonds for 35,000 yuan, 6% Consol bonds for 21,000 yuan, 2.5% Continuance bonds for only 8,000 yuan, and only 4,000 to 5,000 yuan for other bonds. There were no transactions for 7-year bonds or 96 bonds. Although the futures market was quieter compared to the previous week, market sentiment was still considered good, and there was still a substantial amount of trading each day. The first two days of the week were relatively strong, with over 8.7 million yuan on Monday and over 7.7 million yuan on Tuesday. The following days were calmer, with daily trading volume generally around 6 million yuan. The total trading volume for the entire week was 40,670,000 yuan, a decrease of over 11,700,000 yuan compared to the previous week. Tax bureau bonds continued to have the largest volume, accounting for 15,050,000 yuan, divided into 3,625,000 yuan for the March contract and 11,580,000 yuan for the April contract. Rehabilitation bonds also performed well, with 2,370,000 yuan for the March contract and 5,250,000 yuan for the April contract. Continuance bonds had 2,030,000 yuan for the March contract and 5,015,000 yuan for the April contract. 6% Consol bonds had 1,970,000 yuan for the March contract and 2,320,000 yuan for the April contract. 2.5% Continuance bonds only had 2,875,000 yuan, divided into 985,000 yuan for the March contract and 1,890,000 yuan for the April contract. Readjustment bonds had 480,000 yuan for the March contract and 1,760,000 yuan for the April contract. 96 bonds had 415,000 yuan for the March contract and 770,000 yuan for the April contract. The 7-year financial bonds of both types remained very slow, with the 7-year bonds having 135,000 yuan for the March contract and 335,000 yuan for the April contract. The Continuance financial bonds only had 465,000 yuan for the March contract, and there was still no market for the April contract. As for the bond price fluctuations over the past week, on the first day of the week, the market sentiment suddenly became tense due to the tense political situation, and people were weak and unanimously fell. The near-term readjustment bonds decreased by as much as 3.60 yuan, the next month's contract decreased by more than 3 yuan, and the tax bureau futures also fell back by 2.78 yuan. Other bonds fell by 7, 8, or 9 jiao or so. Only financial 96 bonds had minimal fluctuations. On the second day of the week, market sentiment was slightly calmer, and the market took advantage of the low prices to buy, so the prices rose again. The tax bureau and readjustment bond futures both rose by about 1 yuan, and other bonds also improved by 5 or 6 jiao. From then until Friday, the bond market was calm and very stable. Most days there were only fluctuations of a few jiao, which was slightly more advantageous for gains than for losses, and the number was very small. On the last day of the weekend, however, buying interest suddenly increased, and prices rose significantly. The next month's futures for the tax bureau and readjustment bonds each rose by more than 2 yuan, and the rehabilitation futures also improved by 1 yuan and a few jiao. In addition to 96 financial bonds, the others generally increased by about 5 or 6 jiao. As a result, compared to the previous week, except for the near-term futures for readjustment spot and tax bureau spot bonds still falling slightly, the others generally increased slightly. The future of the bond market is still quite gloomy. The statistics on bond price fluctuations over the past week are listed below (unit: yuan)

Yarn Market: Softening Conditions in the Yarn Market Last Week 120

Political situation affects consumption decline

Sellers heavily pressuring, difficult to rebound temporarily

The yarn market was still stable at the beginning of last week, but the trend was weak, which was probably due to the tense political situation. There was a large amount of inventory at the bottom, and there was a risk of decline. Fortunately, the overseas cotton yarn market situation was unanimously trending upward, and people's hearts were strengthened by it. However, the yarn produced in this local market every day is difficult to completely sell off, and there is still a surplus. Moreover, the war has signs of prolongation, so although foreign cotton has risen, local yarn is still difficult to raise. And a portion of large sellers are exerting great pressure, searching the market for 7,000 to 8,000 bales of spot goods in preparation for delivery. With the standard in this situation, it is difficult for the buyers to support, so near-month standard yarn has a crack at the weekend, and the downward trend is more intense. As a result, near-month standard yarn fell by one liang, eight or nine qian to two liang compared to last week, and distant prices fell by four or five qian. The total transaction volume for the entire week was 83,900 bales. Currently, Tianjin, Qingdao, and Sichuan traders are still buying, and others are secondary. Japanese yarn is still hard due to the shortage of goods and sales prices, and local yarn is also flat. It has been found that various traders bought a total of 9,140 bales for the week, and factories opened 2,000+ bales. The following is a record of the purchase volume by various traders:

The River Rice Market in Shanghai Continues to Show Firmness 123

Yesterday, over ten rice boats arrived at the docks in Zhabei. Sales were stable. Early in the morning, the price of Beijing rice was slightly weaker, but because sellers were not eager to sell quickly and avoided being undercut by buyers, they uniformly maintained high asking prices. Therefore, trading volume was low, but the overall market remained firm. The supply of Bo rice was scarce, and sales were steady, with no price increases or decreases. Buying interest in Yangxian rice was quiet. Although some out-of-town merchants inquired about it, they seemed to think the price was too high and were watching the market. Demand for local Xian rice in places like Duzi and Kebu was weak. The market seemed a bit listless, with prices barely holding steady at the original levels. The turnover of Yuan Yin Hua rice was also slow. Fortunately, supply was not heavy, so market prices remained stable.

In South Shanghai, boats arriving at the riverfront were still docking. Sales were not as brisk as the previous day because various rice merchants had already stocked up on Jing rice from Changshu and other places in previous market sessions, so demand was slightly weaker, and prices were stable. Sales of early Bo rice and early rice from places like Qingdao and Sijing along the South Road were not dull, but the goods were moving at steady pace, so the prices also stabilized accordingly. Among them, buyers were very welcome to special high-quality goods. Prices may moderately rise soon. Because of foreign rice, the market conditions for Yang Du Jian rice did not improve, and only ordinary goods were a bit tight. Sales are very active, and inventories will soon be depleted. The future market is difficult to predict. The arrival and sales of Bai Yuan rice are evenly matched, and the situation is quite stable.

Progress in the Silk Market Last Week 124

Japanese Silk More Expensive, European Merchants Abandon Japanese Silk and Seek Chinese Silk

Demand Exceeds Supply, Factories Experience an Increase of Over Ten Taels

Last week, the Shanghai foreign firm silk market turned from firm to rising because Japanese silk prices turned upward after the Japanese government secured a large amount of funds to support silk prices and compensate for losses. Furthermore, gold prices also rose. Since Japan abandoned the gold ban, it has switched to the gold standard, so Japanese silk prices have risen even more, and sales have been stagnant. Silver prices are surprisingly cheap. Chinese silk is still priced in silver taels, so European and American silk merchants are abandoning Japanese silk for Chinese silk. Silk telegrams are successively transferred to Shanghai, and silk sales are smooth. The dry cocoon inventory in Shanghai is low, and it is more than three months before the new cocoons enter the market. There is not much silk, and the supply is about to fall short of demand. In addition, cocoon prices are not loose, and silk costs are still high. Each manufacturer's attitude is firm. The Shanghai factory experienced a sharp increase of more than ten taels. Last week, the foreign firm silk market turned from firm to rising, which is why. A total of more than 500 packages of spot and forward silk were transacted throughout the week, and more than 800 packages were exported. The foreign firms have a total inventory of about 700 packages of silk. Overseas Chinese silk prices are not rising much because Japanese silk prices are turning weak. Ministry Order to Expand the Jianghai Customs Area 125

The Jianghai Customs Superintendent has ordered the Customs Commissioner to comply with the expansion of the Shanghai Jianghai Northern Area. The approval of the Ministry of Finance has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the Ministry of Finance has recently ordered the Jianghai Customs Superintendent, stating that the Shanghai Special Municipality Government had previously consulted that, as proposed by the Shanghai Special Municipality Government Construction Discussion Committee, the committee members Qian Xinzhi and others suggested expanding the Shanghai Customs area. The proposal was submitted to the first meeting of the fourth standing committee, and it was resolved to hand it over to a special task force to review it together with the original proposer. According to the review report, the committee approved the issue of expanding the customs area according to the original proposal. The scope of the expansion should be determined by the municipal government. The proposal was resubmitted to the first meeting of the fifth standing committee, and it was resolved to pass it according to the review report. The original proposal is enclosed. Please determine how to handle it and reply. The original proposal is attached. This is approved. It is noted that Shanghai is the premier commercial port in East Asia, with ships converging and merchants gathering. The proposal to expand the Shanghai Customs area is indeed an urgent plan to revitalize the city and develop industry and commerce. The scope of the expansion, which has now been determined by the Municipal Government based on current needs, extends upstream to Zhangjiatang Port and downstream to Wusong. The corresponding proposal is enclosed and submitted to the Ministry for review. Please quickly instruct the Jianghai Customs Superintendent and the Jianghai Customs Commissioner to comply with and reply. The original proposal is attached. This is approved. It should be noted that, as mentioned in the original proposal, there is indeed a need to expand the Jianghai Customs area. However, whether it is appropriate to extend the expansion scope upstream to Zhangjiatang Port and downstream to Wusong should be clearly investigated and determined. The Customs Administration ordered the Inspectorate General of Customs to survey and map the area and submit it for review. According to the Inspectorate General of Customs' reply, the Customs Administration instructed the Customs Commissioner of Jianghai to comply, conduct a detailed review, and provide detailed maps for review and transfer. The Customs Commissioner of Jianghai, Mei Weiliang, reported that expanding the customs area of the port is indeed an important plan to adapt to the development of the port, and all the sections mentioned in the original consultation of the Shanghai Special Municipality Government are feasible. Based on previous orders, he has drawn detailed maps of the existing area of the port and the areas to be expanded for review. It is noted that the boundaries of the expanded Shanghai Customs area set in the map are appropriate. Based on the previous report, he is enclosing the original map for review. It is noted that the expansion of the customs area has been reviewed and is considered feasible in terms of customs affairs. It should be approved and implemented. The Customs Administration has ordered the Inspectorate General of Customs to comply and publicize it. It is also imperative to transcribe the original proposal sent by the Shanghai Special Municipality Government and order the Customs Superintendent to comply and instruct the Customs Commissioner to publicize it. This order.

Record of the Silk Industry Discussion Conference in Jiangsu and Zhejiang 127

Reporting on Negotiations with the Export Silk Association

Discussing the Settlement of Silk Valuation and Public Weight Inspection

The General Association of Silk Cocoons in Jiangsu, Zhejiang and Anhui convened a discussion conference yesterday (the 22nd) at 3 p.m., gathering silk factory colleagues from various provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to improve the procedures for unwinding silk in foreign firms. Huang Jinchen, Shen Huachen, Zhu Jing'an, Zhu Zhuxian, Sun Rongchang, and others, eighty or ninety people in total, attended. Huang Jinchen and Shen Huachen were elected as the presidium. First, Chairman Huang announced the purpose of the meeting. Then, Chairman Shen stood up to report on the progress of the negotiations on the case, briefly requesting the improvement of silk unwinding procedures, changes in silver collection dates, and the adoption of sample strips. After repeated efforts by myself and Chairman Huang to reason with Mr. Shagu, the chairman of the Export Silk Association, and put forward requirements, we have now received a formal letter in reply from the association, acknowledging the following three points: (1) For consignment silk shipped for export on Saturdays, the silk funds will be paid on Saturday morning; (2) For the adoption of sample strips, only two sample strips are allowed to be drawn for every five pieces of silk; (3) Return of reeling strips. The reeling strips drawn by each foreign firm should be issued with a receipt by the foreign merchant, indicating the number of strips and the quantity. In the future, the manufacturers will use this receipt to recover the reeling strips from the foreign firm and re-weigh the quantity to see if it is compliant. The association has fully accepted the above three points, which has won back a lot of benefits for the industry. The association agreed to immediately instruct all foreign firms to comply. All of our Chinese silk merchants should also strictly implement it and not give up again. Next, the letter from the Export Silk Association requesting two issues was discussed. Because the matter was important, the discussion lasted for a long time. As a result, (1) The foreign merchants requested that the silk should be delivered six days earlier than the agreed month period for unwinding silk in the future. Each manufacturer stated that this matter

Can be said. The public decided to refute the matter with reason. However, when necessary, it can be stated when the transaction is concluded that, with the approval of the factory, the date of delivery should be indicated in the order; otherwise, it will be handled in accordance with the regulations. (2) The foreign merchants requested that the public weight be used to bake 1/1800 pound of silk strips, which is not suitable for exporting in bulk. The case of calculating the value by combining the number of strips and quantities will be resolved by investigating the methods of the Japanese raw silk inspection office as the standard. Finally, Chairman Shen stated that the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has approved the extension of the implementation of the public weight inspection of exported factory silk for one month. The deadline for implementation on April 1 is approaching soon. Each colleague should actively prepare. The meeting adjourned after discussion. It was already six o'clock.

The Department Orders No Arbitrary Fines in Encountered Cases 128

The Shanghai County Government received a letter from the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department stating that the county magistrates and public security bureau chiefs of each county are important local officials, and the county magistrate is especially an official who is close to the people. During this period of political tutelage, how should officials use both authority and virtue to influence and guide the people so that the people can be inspired to participate in revolutionary construction? It is inappropriate to abuse political power and increase the suffering of the people. However, it has been found that in recent years, in cases involving accusations, large fines have been imposed arbitrarily in various counties. Such a situation, even if there is nothing else in the locality, can easily give others grounds for criticism. Therefore, I am issuing a strict warning that you must not arbitrarily impose excessive fines again in the future, or use local public welfare as an excuse to coerce large amounts of donations. You must strictly abide by this. Yesterday, County Magistrate Leng ordered the Public Security Bureau to comply accordingly.

Eleventh District Municipal Committee Petitions for Free Dog Registration 137

Extensive writing emphasizing the necessity of keeping dogs in rural areas

Sincere petition hoping for fundamental solutions to hygiene issues

The municipal committee members of various districts in this city, to petition for the exemption of registration fees for household dogs in order to alleviate the people's hardship, submitted a document to the Health Bureau stating: "Submitting this petition, as per your bureau's Order No. 374, which stated, 'To be obeyed,' upon investigation of the regulations for registering restaurants and household dogs, which have already been promulgated, each rural district should also organize separately to comply with the regulations. However, considering the lower living standards in rural districts, this bureau, in consideration of the residents of rural districts, has already submitted to the municipal government for approval a reduction of half the registration fee (i.e., fifty cents each time). It is now decided that from January 1st to March 1st of the nineteenth year, a two-month registration period will be held. Except for the Wusong and Gaoqiao districts, which should directly submit their applications to the health model district offices in those areas, all restaurants and household dogs in the Yin'hang, Zhenru, Pusong, Fahua, Caojing, Tangqiao, Luhang, Pengpu, Yangsi, and Jiangwan districts must uniformly report to the municipal committee members of their respective districts and pay the fees, which should be compiled and submitted to this bureau once every ten days for review before permits are issued. Besides issuing separate orders and proclamations, the municipal committee members of each district are hereby ordered to comply and implement this order." Upon receiving this order, except for the restaurant registration, which has already been handled separately and reported to your bureau, the committee members believe that the collection of fees for household dog registration is absolutely unacceptable. We respectfully submit this to the director. Upon investigation, most of the households in each district are farmers. Taking Zhenru district as an example, out of a total of 5,410 households in the entire district, 4,524 are farming households, accounting for more than 83% of the total. And seven or eight out of ten farming households keep dogs. The usefulness of dogs is to supplement the inadequacy of police force. Dogs are loyal to their duty and are exceptionally alert. Upon hearing any sound, they bark incessantly, and the owner, upon hearing the sound, prepares for it. Therefore, thieves often hesitate to target homes that keep dogs. Moreover, in the event of bandits committing robbery, a dog barks wildly, and other dogs echo, and nearby villagers, upon hearing the alarm, inform each other, rise up to resist, and the bandits retreat. This is the usefulness of dogs. Therefore, rural people love dogs as much as Arabs love horses, treating them as family members. Even extremely poor households, struggling to make ends meet, often enjoy keeping dogs. Now, the number of households that keep dogs is not small, and the usefulness of dogs is so great. However, your bureau has a decree for registering household dogs and a collection fee of fifty cents per head and a one-cent stamp tax. For the entire city, the amount must be considerable. However, in handling government affairs, it is important to have a purpose. What is the purpose of holding household dog registration? If it is to prevent rabid and ferocious dogs from biting people, then it is enough to order dog owners to keep their dogs tied up in one place during the day, preventing them from roaming freely, or to add muzzles to prevent them from biting. This can achieve the purpose, and there is no need to register them door-to-door.

With extreme freedom, rabid and ferocious dogs still bite people as before. What benefit is there to public health? If it is for collecting people's wealth, then in this time of consecutive years of famine, most farmers in the suburbs cannot make ends meet even from one morning to the next. This six-cent registration fee is the equivalent of five days' worth of grain for the poor. Now, to collect it because of keeping dogs, is it not inevitable that the farmers will react and feel resentment? It is still remembered that when the rebel Sun Chuanfang stole power and Ding Wenjiang was appointed as the Shanghai-Songhu Superintendent, under the guise of implementing new policies, a household tax of twenty cents for doorplates was collected in the Tangqiao district, which caused the villagers to beat gongs and gather crowds, destroying the homes of those in charge. The situation was turbulent and unapproachable, and those who talked about it still changed color. Is the amount now several times that amount? Reading Tang Zhen's "Enriching the People" chapter, it says, "Wealth is the treasure of the country and the life of the people. Treasure cannot be stolen, and life cannot be robbed. Sages treat the people as their children and grandchildren and the four seas as their treasury. They do not steal their treasure or rob their life, so every family is prosperous, and wives and children are peaceful." It also says, "Those who take by abuse will lose a hundred gold for taking one gold, and lose a hundred rooms for taking one room." Therefore, Confucius had the saying that "oppressive government is fiercer than a tiger," which clearly shows the future. How can we not fear it? How can we not be careful? The way to hygiene is multifaceted. Not observing the pits and toilets in each district, which are located on thoroughfares, with foul odors steaming, and maggots gathering. The tributaries and interrupted harbors, with water as black as ink, and foul odors unbearable. Between summer and autumn, epidemics spread. Because there are no hospitals, there is no way to treat them. People infect each other, and the dead are piled on top of each other. Those with a little heart cannot bear it. For the sake of the people's health, it seems that these matters should be addressed first, seeking fundamental solutions. These matters are ten or a hundred times more important than dog registration. The committee members have studied the municipal administrations of various countries, but they can still distinguish whether the application is suitable for the environment or not. Now, the concession has dog registration and dog permit procedures because densely populated areas are not suitable for raising dogs. Therefore, there are measures to limit it. Now, to apply it to remote rural areas is obviously unsuitable for the current environment. Reading Qu You's line, "The master only needs to guard the door, avoiding the labor of chasing Korean dogs for hunting," it is clear that rural people cannot live without dogs for a day. We dare to humbly submit to Director Hu, requesting to change the method of dog registration, allowing it to be free to alleviate the people's hardship, which would truly be for the public's convenience. Respectfully submitted to Hu, Director of the Shanghai Special Municipality Health Bureau, by Yang Xinzheng, Municipal Committee Member of Caojing District, Hong Lanxiang of Zhenru, Wang Shouyu, Zhang Qiwen of Luhang, Yang Hongjun of Fahua, Zhong Renjie of Gaoqiao, Chen Yafu of Pusong, Wu Xuen of Jiangwan, Yan Enzuo, Liu Ziwen of Wusong, Pan Wuding of Gaohang, Zhou Nianzu of Pengpu, Ling Zhibin, Zhu Zonglu of Yinhang, Zhu Jiajun, Wang Hui of Tangqiao, and Chen Tianxi of Yangsi.

Jisheng Society's Disaster Relief Report in Beiping Nankou 139

This port's Chinese Jisheng Society recently received a report from She Jungsheng, director of the disaster relief office stationed in Tianjin, stating that the 24 villages in the eighth district of Beiping Nankou reported that the villages along the mountain range in Nankou Fuxingzhuang suffered a rare disaster last year. Regardless of wealth or poverty, all suffered from famine. Families had no stone's worth of grain, and their homes were empty. Brothers, wives, and children were scattered, and the old and weak were dying in ditches. Fortunately, the Shanghai Chinese Jisheng Society showed great compassion and provided disaster relief. Over the past few months, time and again, the famine victims have received great kindness. However, as winter ends and spring arrives, all the grain seeds have been exhausted, and only one or two out of a hundred plowing oxen and horses are still alive. There is no way to sow seeds. Now, at this time of year when the old grain is depleted and the new grain has not yet arrived, the famine victims have no way to make plans. They earnestly request extra kindness and continued spring relief to help them through this difficult time. Once the autumn harvest is promising, they can celebrate their survival, which is all due to the great virtue of your society, etc. Since last winter, the society has provided disaster relief in Nankou three times, spending a considerable amount of money. Now, they are requesting a fourth spring relief. If the society agrees, its resources will be stretched thin. If it refuses, its previous efforts will be in vain. A detailed letter has been sent to Director She Guisheng, stating that after the 600 big stones of grain and corn from the three Nankou relief efforts have been transported and distributed, a thorough investigation should be conducted to determine how many people are still unable to survive without relief and how much grain is actually lacking, and then a decision should be made to maintain the current situation and alleviate the suffering.

Henan Provincial Relief Committee kowtows." Fire on Hopeland Road 143

The home of Lu Fudi, who runs a straw business on Hopeland Road in Zhujiaqiao, West Shanghai, caught fire around 6:00 PM on the 22nd (the day before yesterday) due to carelessness with fire while cooking. Suddenly, thick smoke billowed out and burst through the roof. The fire brigade rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm, but the fire had already spread to the straw piles, and the fire was raging. The firefighters worked hard to extinguish the fire, and it was finally extinguished. A total of two houses and over a hundred bundles of straw were burned. The police from the sixth district were dispatched to the scene and took the fire's source, Lu Fudi (age 28), and associates Xu Amei (age 34) and Zhang Zhifa (age 43), back to the district for interrogation.

Gold Shop Apprentice Suspected of Arson 145

Plot to Embezzle 5,000 Gold Failed

Detained on Suspicion of Arson

Xing Ximing, a native of Jiangyin, who is not yet twenty years old, was recommended by relatives to work at Tongli Gold Shop, No. 4 Museum Road, last year. He was quite intelligent and was liked by his superiors. A few days ago, the shop accountant ordered him to call Chunyuan Money Shop to get 5,000 taels of silver. Xing took this opportunity to order 10,000 taels in the call. When the money was delivered, Xing gave 5,000 taels to the accountant. Xing embezzled the remaining 5,000 taels, which was a term draft, and took it as his own. He then took the draft to Chunyuan Shop, hoping to cash it. Because he was not familiar with the cashing procedure, he inevitably revealed flaws. The shop clerk immediately called Tongli to inquire, and Xing's scheme was foiled. He returned to the shop in frustration. The shop owner, Sun Dongchuan, thought that he was young and ignorant and gave him a slight reprimand as a warning. However, on the night before last, a fire suddenly broke out in Tongli's office. Fortunately, it was discovered immediately, and water was used to extinguish it, avoiding a major conflagration. Sun Dongchuan investigated the matter in detail afterward and felt that Xing was very suspicious of the fire or that he had deliberately set the fire. He reported to the General Inspector's Office and sent detectives to arrest Xing. The next day, he was sent to the Provisional Court for investigation. According to Xing's confession, he woke up late at night, defecated, sat by the table, and took a cigarette to smoke. Then Mr. Fang came in. Fearing being blamed, he secretly threw the remaining cigarette under the table. Unexpectedly, a fire suddenly broke out afterward. He immediately took water to extinguish it and did not intentionally set the fire, etc. He hired lawyer Jiang Rong to defend him and requested bail. Judge Gao ordered the defendant to pay a bail of 300 yuan and rescheduled the hearing.

News from Various Trade Unions 146

The Tea Trade Union held its third re-election meeting at 1:00 PM on the 21st, with over 100 member representatives attending. Chairman Zhu Runbin conducted the meeting and observed the rituals. First, Chairman Zhu Runbin reported on the purpose of the meeting, and the executive committee reported on the progress of the union's affairs. Finally, proposals were discussed: (A) Proposals from Comrade Zhu Runbin: (1) Expedite the reorganization of various branches to strengthen the foundation. Resolved: Approved. (2) Establish a job placement office. Resolved: Approved. (3) Create a Tea Trade Union Monthly to promote and publicize domestic products. Resolved: Approved. (4) Establish a tea trade evening school and a school for the children of workers. Resolved: Approved. (5) Advise various groups with resources and engaged in the tea industry to seek to improve the methods of Chinese tea production to implement Sun Yat-sen's policy of saving the country through industry. Resolved: Handed over to the publicity department for extensive publicity. (6) Petition the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to order all tea-producing areas in various provinces to improve the methods of Chinese tea production. Resolved: Approved. (B) Proposals from Comrade Guo Ganting: (1) Draft regulations to protect members working outside the city and request retroactive approval. Resolved: Approved. (2) Draft regulations for member self-governance and request approval. Resolved: Approved. (3) Draft regulations for disciplining members and request approval. Resolved: Approved. (C) Proposals from Comrade Yu Kongbin: (1) Those without a relevant history in the tea industry shall not be allowed to act as foremen. Resolved: Approved. (2) New members joining the union in the third session shall pay an additional three yuan in addition to the membership fee to replenish the union's funds. Resolved: Approved. (D) Proposals from Comrade Jiang Fuyuan: (1) Request that employers provide year-round meals for the four pillars (senior workers) and four supports (intermediate workers). Resolved: Approved. (2) The union's annual expenditure is huge and should reduce the number of standing committee members. Resolved: The union's standing committee members are already set in accordance with the trade union organization law, and this item should not be discussed. (3) The gatekeepers and foremen of each warehouse have already appointed their relatives, but when their relatives have not yet arrived in Shanghai, the position shall not be filled by workers temporarily. If they want to fill it temporarily, it must be for a period of one year. Resolved: Approved. (E) Proposals from Comrade Cheng Yinfu: The union's investigation committee should diligently investigate working hours to alleviate the suffering of workers. Resolved: Approved. (2) The union shall never reveal the names of reporters when workers come to the union to report to avoid dismissal. Resolved: The union has a responsibility to protect them. Workers should not worry. (F) Proposals from Comrade Yu Yusheng: (1) Foremen shall not hold other positions concurrently. Resolved: Approved. (2) The allowance for pickers cannot be transferred to fans, and the allowance for fans shall be requested from employers at five cents per worker. Resolved: Approved. (3) Many workers did not receive benefits in the previous session, and the current session must investigate and punish them. Resolved: Approved. After discussion, ballots were cast, and Wu Bochao, Cheng Ganting, Hu Mingsheng, Yu Kongbao, Zhu Runbin, Yu Naigeng, Hong Xinyuan, Hong Zhonghe, Yu Qintai, Cheng Pinzi, Jiang Fuyuan, Yu Guozhen, Cheng Maochun, Li Futian, Ye Tiansheng and other fifteen people were elected as executive committee members. Foreign Press Discusses Japanese and the Municipal Council 147

Chinese Citizens Must Maintain Strict Surveillance

The *Millard's Review*, translated by the World News Agency, states: According to reports, the Japanese Road Business Association of Shanghai has sent a letter to the Public Concession's Municipal Council, requesting three things: (1) Increase the number of police officers within the Concession to 500; (2) Increase the use of senior Japanese police officers in the Police Department; (3) The authority and treatment of Japanese officers in the Police Department should be equal to those of other foreign officers. This report seems to be in line with the words of former Municipal Council Chairman Arnold in his letter published in the previous issue of this newspaper. According to Arnold, the reason for his failure in the last Municipal Council election was that he had rejected the Japanese's demands (disproportionate increase in Japanese police and other matters), so the Japanese cast opposing votes against him, preventing him from being re-elected. Arnold also said that if the British in the Concession do not come out to vote in large numbers, the municipal administration will be controlled by the Japanese election machine). After Arnold's letter was published, an unnamed Japanese national (spokesperson) denied his statement, saying that the Japanese did not oppose the increase in the number of Chinese members of the Municipal Council (but of course, the Chinese directors should not be in the majority), etc. Observing these words of the Japanese, their intentions are clearly revealed, that is, the Japanese currently have greater representation and police power, and they do not want any increase in Chinese power. This kind of request from the Japanese can be ignored, but there are many foreigners (Europeans and Americans) in the Public Concession who would rather agree to the Japanese's requests than the Chinese's requests. In other words, these foreigners would rather trade with the Japanese, increasing the Japanese's power in the Municipal Council and the Police Department, than see the Chinese gain a controlling voice in the Concession. This is the key to the overall situation, and the Chinese should pay close attention to it. Although the election in the Municipal Council appeared to be open, it was actually conducted in secret. The oppressive situation imposed by the Japanese as stated in Arnold's letter has obviously been the case for a long time, but Arnold is only speaking about it now, and the public in Shanghai is only learning about it now. In that case, among the directors elected this time, there may be those who have significant obligations to the Japanese. The three Japanese requests mentioned above may have originated from this. We must strictly monitor this scene of Municipal Council politics, otherwise, one day the Municipal Council will transfer the Concession not back to the Chinese, but to the Japanese. Only when it has become a fact will we wake up as if from a dream.

Robbery Using Anesthetic Powder 148

Able to Make the Victim Unconscious

Thief Shen A'jin Arrested

Shen A'jin, a habitual thief from Shaoxing, was carrying a package when he passed through Rue Amiral Bayle in the French Concession a few days ago. He was spotted by detectives Lu Zhulin and Mao Jingen from the special division of the French Concession Police, who arrested Shen and seized the stolen goods. Upon opening the package, the chief detective found a white lambskin robe, gold bracelets, gold chains, and banknotes, worth over 700 yuan. A small packet of anesthetic powder was also found on Shen's person. Under interrogation, Shen confessed that he had stolen the items from the Senchang pawnshop at 90 Avenue de l'Observatoire. He also revealed that twenty-seven pieces of foreign cloth had been taken to the Chinese area and pawned by his accomplice, Shen Changlin. When asked about the purpose of the powder, Shen replied that he used it during robberies by lighting the powder, causing the victims to become unconscious. The chief detective, having obtained the confession, ordered Shen to be detained. He also instructed detectives to arrest Shen Changlin in the Chinese area, recover the stolen goods, and bring him back to the police station. It was further discovered that the thieves had stolen three leather coats from Pan Youliang's house at 1 Rue Pingji Li last month, which were pawned for spending money. Therefore, the victims were summoned to the French Concession Court the day before yesterday to prosecute Shen and his gang. The plaintiffs, Min Ruizhi and Pan Youliang, testified about the theft, stating that the defendants had broken into their houses. Although they were initially aware of the intrusion, their bodies became paralyzed, and they soon fell unconscious, fearing that the thieves had used anesthetic drugs. They requested severe punishment. When questioned, Shen A'jin claimed that the stolen goods were actually stolen by Wang A'rong, who was still at large, while offering evasive answers. Shen Changlin claimed that he only helped with pawning and did not participate in the theft. The judge, Mr. Zhu, ordered the defendants to be detained for further investigation.

Conflict Between Workers and Militia Members in Xijialong 149

Caused by Stealing Vegetables

Militia Member Zhang Injured

Yesterday at approximately 1:00 PM, a conflict occurred in Xijialong, located one and a half li north of Zhenru in the western suburbs of Shanghai near Caojiadu. Over one hundred Jiangbei workers clashed with militia members due to the theft of vegetables by the workers. One militia member was injured and a rifle and a row of bullets were seized. The details of the incident are recorded below:

Cause of the Incident: Recently, vegetables and bamboo shoots grown by villagers near Zhenru have been frequently stolen by groups of Jiangbei workers, causing significant losses to the villagers. As a result, the Zhenru district militia often sends out patrols to protect the crops. Yesterday at approximately 1:00 PM, Lin Xiao'erzi, a Jiangbei worker employed at a certain oil factory, was caught stealing vegetables from a field in Xijialong. He was spotted by a militia member who tried to stop him and question him. However, the worker not only refused to comply but immediately gathered four or five workers to cause trouble.

Workers Gather: The district militia headquarters, fearing that the workers' ignorance would lead to trouble, dispatched over ten militia members to mediate. However, workers already rushed back to the oil factory (which was closed for Sunday) and immediately gathered over one hundred workers, some carrying shoulder poles, some with pistols, some with iron bars, and some with bayonets, creating a menacing atmosphere.

A Fierce Fight: Once the workers arrived at the location, they swarmed upon the militia members, attacking them and firing several pistol shots. Seeing the unfavorable situation, the militia members also fired two shots while retreating. The militia headquarters then dispatched over ten more militia members to provide reinforcements. The workers bravely kidnapped a militia member named Zhang Jingshan and dispersed. The militia members immediately pursued and captured six leading workers, who were brought back to the militia headquarters. It was not yet clear whether they had fired the shots that injured people.

Severe Beating of Militia Member: Militia member Zhang Jingshan was kidnapped by the workers, who dragged him away while beating him. They took him behind the oil factory and seized his rifle, a row of bullets, an armed belt, and his badge number. His uniform was torn to shreds. The militia member was then tied to a telephone pole and subjected to relentless kicking and punching. As the crowd of onlookers grew, the workers scattered and fled. The militia member suffered head injuries that caused profuse bleeding, and sustained multiple injuries on his body, leading to unconsciousness.

Police Dispatched for Rescue: Tai Zurong, the platoon leader of the second platoon of the first company of the militia, immediately reported the incident to the Sixth District Police Station. Section Chief Duan dispatched Head Constable Hu from the Second Precinct along with police officers, but the workers had already fled. They rescued militia member Zhang Jingshan and brought him back to the station. Section Chief Duan questioned the militia member, who stated that he was thirty years old, lived in Xijialong, made a living by farming, and was a member of the 61st militia. Section Chief Duan, noting that the militia member was severely injured, granted Platoon Leader Qin permission to take him back for medical treatment. It was reported that three or four other militia members were also injured.

Four Thieves Arrested, Admitting Their Crimes Without Reservation

Pistol Retrieved From Under Roof Tiles in Yunzhou Inn

Xu, the captain of the Shanghai Special City Public Security Bureau's water patrol team, discovered that the thieves involved in the robbery of 5,000 yuan in foreign currency from the Longtoufang at the Shanghai North Railway Station were frequently seen at the Zhongxin Teahouse on North Sixth Road in the city. Lecture at the YMCA Yesterday 151

Sex Problems and Youth

Yesterday marked the third lecture of the academic lecture series held by the Sichuan Road YMCA, titled "Sex Problems and Youth." Both men and women attended enthusiastically. The speaker was Dr. Eddy from the United States, and the translation was provided by Mr. Wu Zengyu, with shorthand recording by Bingxun National Phonetic Speedometer Society. The gist of the lecture is recorded below. Before us lies a very important and difficult problem, namely the issue of sex, which is most closely related to us. In the past, however, we have suffered greatly because we have neglected this important issue and have not paid attention to it. There are two driving forces in life: hunger and love. One is the struggle for survival, and the other is the war of love. These two forces can make people succeed or fail. Sex can lead to bad things, but with proper guidance and rules, it can become a very good thing. It all depends on whether we are the masters of sex or are controlled by it. What is sex? It is the mutual love between men and women who are physiologically different, forming families and filling them with joy. We should regard sex as the most beautiful, the most sacred, and the noblest thing in life. There are two extremes in the issue of sex: excessive indulgence and excessive restraint. Both can lead to unhappiness. Because sex is the greatest driving force in life, gradually growing and expanding in scope, education should start from the family. Otherwise, bad children will also corrupt others. A person who receives good sex education can have a strong body and achieve success in their career. Washington was able to succeed because he paid attention to sex education. At the time, there was a very intelligent person of similar status who turned into a traitor because he did not pay attention to sex issues. Mazzini said that no unchaste person can be a true patriot. Often, a person who contracts a venereal disease harms their wife, a truly great sin. Therefore, young people must maintain their purity. Sex can elevate or lower one's character, build up or destroy. Young people, do not lose your wisdom, and let wisdom guide you throughout your life. Maintain your purity. This afternoon at 5:30 PM, Dr. Eddy will continue his lecture at the YMCA, titled "The Choice Between the Sexes."

Marriage Disputes Over Transactional Marriages 152

Zhang Zhongyi Eager to Marry

Zhu Dasheng Finds It Difficult to Act as Matchmaker

Zhang Zhongyi, a villager from Xinjing Jiangqiao in the northwest suburbs of Shanghai, is approaching thirty and still unmarried. Zhu Dasheng approached him recently, claiming to have a woman from Taicang named Wang Suyun, who is twenty-two years old and whose mother wished to arrange her marriage. The dowry was very low, which suited Zhang's wishes. However, he needed to see her in person. Zhu brought Suyun to Zhang's house, and Zhang was delighted after seeing her. He asked Zhu to help arrange the marriage. Zhu was even more accommodating and willing to let Suyun move in first. He asked Zhang to pay 80 yuan as a deposit to inform her mother, Wang Wangshi, to come to Shanghai to discuss the marriage. This was entirely a transactional arrangement, but Zhang was so overjoyed that he forgot his concerns and acted accordingly. A few days later, Zhu Dasheng suddenly arrived at Zhang's house with Wang Wangshi, who claimed that she did not want her daughter to marry Zhang. Zhang was greatly alarmed and tried to negotiate, which was noticed by a patrolman, who questioned them and arrested them all, bringing them to the First Precinct of the Sixth District. After interrogation, as they were about to be handed over, Zhang and Wang Wangshi agreed to get married after discussing it in the detention center. The police, seeing that the case had an unclear background and that marriage should not be treated as a commercial transaction, ordered that the police station could not resolve the matter and handed them over to the local court for investigation yesterday.

Detectives Yang A'quan and Bao Tan Sun Shaokun from the Harbin police force arrested the robbers, Lai Guiquan and Hou A'bao, who then implicated their accomplices. Subsequently, Chen Yunsheng, Wang Lisheng, Chen Jinmei, Zhou Lifu, Shen Liansheng, Chen Xiasheng, and a woman named Liang Ge'shi were arrested. Two pistols and over one hundred bullets were seized. It was discovered that, apart from Wang Lisheng, Chen Jinmei, and Shen Liansheng, the others had robbed the homes of Lu Zhangzhang at 1264 Route Robert, Pan Songhe at 11 Xiaoshadu Road, and Wu Shoushan at 1204 Route Hude between December 27th of last year and the 6th of this month. The robbers even fired shots when they robbed Wu's house, intending to kill the owner. Yesterday, the victims and witnesses were summoned, and the robbers were handed over to the provisional court. Judge Ge interrogated them. The police lawyer requested the withdrawal of charges against Wang Lisheng and two others. The court granted the request, ordering Wang Lisheng, Chen Jinmei, and Shen Liansheng to be released. The others were remanded in custody for further questioning at a later date.

Disposition of Assets of Northwest Bank – Question Submitted to Supreme Command by the Court 155

When Feng Yuxiang betrayed the Central Government last summer, the Provisional Court, upon orders, sealed up the Northwest Bank's Shanghai financial institution, ordering the police to temporarily oversee all of its assets, pending instructions from Commander-in-Chief Jiang. Over half a year has passed, and the Supreme Command has not issued any instructions regarding the disposition of assets, so they remain under police custody. The police lawyer filed a petition in court the day before yesterday, seeking instructions on how to dispose of the bank's assets. Judge Gao instructed the lawyer that the court intended to submit another request to the Supreme Command regarding the disposition of assets and would notify the police upon receiving orders from the Command. The lawyer acknowledged the instruction and left.

Police Meddling in Chinese Territory 156

Bu A'er and Two Chinese Constables Ignore Propriety

Around 8 PM last night, Bu A'er, a Shandong man who sells flatbread, went to Ai Hua Inn, located at 346 North Zhejiang Road in Chinese territory. The counter clerk, Mr. Huang, instructed the bellboy to take him upstairs, stating that the room rate was 1 jiao 5 fen. Bu insisted on staying downstairs and only wanted to pay 1 jiao. The landlady, seeing the anger on Bu's face, agreed. However, Bu then complained about the crowd downstairs and demanded the return of his room fee before leaving. Two patrol constables from the Huisi police station happened to pass by, and Bu falsely reported that the inn had beaten and evicted him. The two constables believed Bu's story and went to the inn to question them. Bu then punched and attacked the counter clerk, Mr. Huang, intending to drag him outside. The bellboy tried to dissuade him, but the constables aided Bu in his assault and even brandished their guns. Seeing this, the lodgers realized that this was Chinese territory and the concession police had no right to interfere. They locked the iron bars on the glass windows, intending to report the incident to nearby Chinese police via the back door. At this moment, Bu and the two constables forcefully pushed the windows, causing them to collapse, shattering the glass. The broken glass fell on Bu's head and face, causing him to bleed profusely. The two constables, seeing an opportunity, arrested Huang, the two bellboys, and Bu A'er, bringing them to the Huisi police station. The police chief, after learning that the incident occurred in Chinese territory, rebuked them all and instructed the two constables that the concession should not interfere in disputes that occur in Chinese territory to avoid misunderstandings and damaging relations. They were then released and left. By the time the Chinese police arrived, Bu A'er had already fled. The inn immediately reported the details of the incident to the Chinese police to be forwarded to the relevant Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Theft Case at Wusong Zhonggong School 157

Investigation Uncovers Suspicions of Reactionary Activities

Xu Jingping, a student at Wusong Zhonggong School, living in Room 8 of the dormitory, discovered that 220 yuan in banknotes had disappeared from his clothing chest when he checked it on the morning of the 14th of this month. The clothes and other items in the chest were untouched, and none of his roommates had lost anything. Greatly alarmed, Xu immediately reported the incident to the dormitory director for investigation. However, no trace of the money could be found. You Shizhi, the principal of the school, believing the matter concerned the reputation of the entire school, sent a letter to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday. District Chief Chen Youxin immediately dispatched detectives Yu Peifa and Tang Bingxiang to investigate Room 8 in the dormitory. They found no signs of forced entry on the doors, windows, or walls, and the clothing chest was intact, determining that the theft was not committed by an outsider but by an insider. They prepared a report and then summoned the victim and school officials Zhu Mingda and Lu Weishan to the station. District Officer Li questioned them. Xu testified that he was 22 years old and from Ningbo. He brought a total of 850 yuan when he came to Shanghai from his hometown. He deposited 250 yuan with his relative, Hong Xingji (living at 79 Huaxing Lane, Hongxingfang, Baoshan Road), lent 150 yuan to a friend from Hangzhou, Xu Xiaogong, spent 35 yuan on books, 110 yuan on clothing and miscellaneous expenses, and 105 yuan on tuition fees, leaving him with 220 yuan. He wrapped the money in paper and hid it in his chest. He checked the chest on the 12th and saw that the money was still there. However, when he checked again on the 14th, only the wrapping paper remained, and the money was gone. He then reported the incident to the dormitory director. There were four people in the room: Deng Zhongbang, Huang Kaihua, and Zhang Guohui, all from Guangdong. Zhang was arrested in Shanghai on the 8th for distributing reactionary leaflets and has been sent to the Suzhou High Court. Deng visited Zhang on the 13th. After discovering the theft on the 14th, Xu went to investigate but found that Zhang had been sent to Suzhou that day. Therefore, he does not know whether Deng went with him. The dormitory attendant in charge of the room is Zhu Mingda. Although Xu cannot say that he stole the money, he should be held responsible and requested an investigation. Zhu Mingda testified that he was 27 years old and from Xuzhou. He was in charge of eleven rooms, including the room where Mr. Xu and the others lived. There were many people coming and going, so he did not lock the doors, making it difficult to manage. Lu Weishan was called in to help, and Zhu always accompanied him when he went to the students' rooms, never letting him go alone. He did not know about the theft of Mr. Xu's money and asked for forgiveness. Lu Weishan testified that he was 29 years old and from Yangzhou. Zhu Mingda called him to help, and Zhu accompanied him when he went to the students' rooms. He did not know about the theft of Mr. Xu's money and asked for forgiveness. After reviewing the testimonies, District Officer Li believed that it was necessary to investigate whether Xu, a student who brought over 800 yuan, deposited and borrowed a large portion of it, was telling the truth. Furthermore, Zhang Guohui, a roommate, was arrested in Shanghai for distributing reactionary leaflets, and Deng Zhongbang did not avoid suspicion and visited him. Therefore, it was necessary to investigate whether Deng and Huang were involved. He reported the information to District Chief Chen, planning to go to Zhonggong School that night with District Officer Li and the original detectives, with the consent of the school's dormitory director, to search Room 8. Two letters from Xu Xiaogong of Hangzhou were found in the victim's chest, confirming that Xu had brought a large sum of money to prepare for mining and that the money borrowed from his friend was factual. Detectives were dispatched to investigate Hong Xingji's residence on Baoshan Road, and it was reported that 250 yuan had indeed been deposited there, confirming Xu's loss. In Deng Zhongbang's suitcase under his bed, a newly carved square seal was found, reading "Chapter of the Summer School of Fudan University" and a personal seal of "Li Denghui," as well as four wooden seals with the inscriptions "Mingsue," "Socialism," "ABB," and "Economic Problems in China." Deng claimed that the suitcase and its contents were left by his classmate, Liu Yaoxian, who lived in the Shanghai branch of the school. Huang Kaihua was found to be beyond suspicion. District Officer Li believed that the large number of seals found were reactionary and that the case was serious. He immediately took Deng and the seals back to the Seventh District Office for further investigation. Deng testified that he was 24 years old and from Guangdong. He did not know that Liu had left such seals in the suitcase and asked for investigation. After reviewing the testimony, District Officer Li immediately reported to the District Chief of the adjacent district, ordered the arrest of Zhu Mingda, who was related to the theft case, and released Lu Weishan. At the same time, he ordered the detectives to investigate and arrest the thieves and bring them to justice. The reactionary suspicion case was also assigned to detectives yesterday to arrest Liu Huixian for strict investigation, and a written report was submitted to the Public Security Bureau for review.

Unmarried Woman Gives Birth to a Child 158

500 Yuan to Terminate the Marriage

Two-Way Payment for the Three-Year-Old Child

Through the introduction of a matchmaker, Chen Huifang was promised to He Longgen. They had not yet married but had already cohabited and had a son, who is now three years old. Chen Huifang repeatedly urged her husband to hold a formal wedding, but He not only refused but also abandoned her. Chen Huifang then hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in court, requesting a divorce and compensation for maintenance expenses. After repeated summonses, the defendant claimed that he could not afford the marriage due to poverty.
